Extremely Severe Wind and Storm in US and Mexico 87

Hundreds of Thousands Homeless

Material Losses Reach Millions

(New York) News received here today indicates that the storms that struck the Mexican coast and the New England states yesterday caused many deaths and injuries. In San Luis Potosi, Tamaulipas, 45 people were killed or injured, and 156,000 people were left homeless. Soldiers are currently searching for the victims. Fourteen female corpses and fourteen children's corpses have already been recovered today, as well as nine male corpses. The estimated loss is in the millions of dollars. North Carolina was the hardest hit, with 15 deaths and many missing. Countless people were left homeless, and property damage reached millions of dollars. All New England states except Massachusetts were affected by the wind and rain, and the losses were considerable. However, Pennsylvania, New York, and New Jersey were spared. (19th Reuters Dispatch)

Hurricane Hits Japan 88

Osaka: This morning, there were strong winds and rain in the Kyushu area. The waves were very high in the Genkai Strait and the Sea of Japan. Fire ships from Moji and Shimonoseki to China and Korea returned halfway. Both the morning and evening shifts of the Shimonoseki-Busan connecting ships were suspended. The connecting ship scheduled to leave Nagasaki for Shanghai today will also be postponed. The wind has become more intense this afternoon. (19th Hualian Dispatch)

(Tokyo) Since the morning of Sunday, a hurricane has blown through Okinawa Island, resulting in the destruction of 1,300 houses, the sinking of 17 fishing boats, and 11 missing. There has been considerable damage to farmland and orchards. The hurricane is now in Kyushu. All ship traffic, including the ferry between Moji and Busan, has been suspended. (19th Reuters Dispatch)

Poland and Danzig Sign Two Important Agreements 89

A Major Problem in Eastern European Politics Temporarily Resolved

National Telegraph from Danzig, 18th: An agreement was reached between the Free City of Danzig and Poland on August 5th of this year, and the application of the Port of Danzig was re-defined by the two countries, giving greater convenience to Poland's imports and exports. A treaty regarding this agreement was signed again today. This treaty detailed the terms that Poland was willing to accept. Poland's intention was to prevent the reduction of Polish commercial transportation using the Port of Danzig. Since the signing of this agreement, certain commodities can be exclusively used the Port of Danzig as a transportation hub. This agreement will terminate on September 30th of next year, and it will automatically expire if both parties do not agree to continue it in advance. Furthermore, signed at the same time as this agreement was an agreement on the treatment of Poles residing in the Free City of Danzig. These two agreements are of great importance to the stability of Eastern European politics. Therefore, after the establishment of the two agreements, Poland and Danzig can probably coexist peacefully for a period of time.

To Reopen on the Fifth of Next Month

Havas Dispatch from London, 19th: According to the (Financial News), negotiations between Britain and the United States on the war debt issue have been scheduled to reopen on October 5th.

Serious Epidemic in Northern Manchuria 91

(Dalian) It is reported that a serious epidemic has occurred in northern Manchuria. More than 600 people have died in the past half month. It is reported that some have died of plague and some have died of pneumonic plague. The South Manchuria Railway Company announced today that the epidemic is most prevalent in Sipingjie and Taonan. Rat extermination propaganda has begun there, leather trade has been suspended, and trains to Taonan and Kaitong have been suspended to prevent the epidemic from spreading. South Manchuria has now adopted strict medical restrictions to prevent the spread of the epidemic. (19th Reuters Dispatch)

U.S. Government to Expand Lending Procedures 92

Cotton Industry Unanimously Requests Currency Inflation

Roosevelt Signs New Mining Industry Regulations

Reuters Dispatch from Washington, 18th: President Roosevelt today allocated another $150 million from the Treasury for the Financial Reconstruction Corporation to expand lending procedures, due to Southern congressmen advocating a straightforward inflation of cotton prices. Bank operations are currently restricted by a large number of cotton documents. In the future, new government funds will be used to assist them. Financial Reconstruction Corporation Chairman Jones announced the new plan. The currency inflation movement has gained the greatest momentum since Congress authorized the President to issue new currency or devalue the dollar. People in the cotton industry and key figures in the Southern parties met here, making currency inflation one of President Roosevelt's biggest problems. Oklahoma Senator Thomas recently notified Congress, asking it to express its views on inflation. He has received a hundred replies, with only four opposing inflation. Thomas now says he will convene a meeting to elect a committee to convey Congress's views on inflation to the President. All cotton-producing states will participate in this meeting.

Reuters Dispatch from Washington, 18th: The American Cotton Industry Conference today unanimously passed a resolution requesting President Roosevelt to use his power to implement currency inflation in order to raise the price of cotton to two cents per pound and cottonseed to thirty dollars per ton.

Reuters Dispatch from Washington, 18th: After obtaining the consent of all parties in the coal industry, President Roosevelt signed the coal mining industry regulations at the White House today. The President is currently suffering from a cold and has not left the White House. The industry regulations stipulate a 40-hour work week for bituminous coal mining and set minimum wages for skilled and unskilled workers. They also stipulate that sales prices will be negotiated by the coal industry under the supervision of the National Recovery Administration. The industry regulations also provide for the establishment of a mechanism for public arbitration of labor disputes. President Roosevelt deleted the clauses relating to labor rights because labor leaders opposed them. The industry regulations will be implemented in October. At the same time, no less than 19 labor disputes have been resolved under the supervision of the National Recovery Act in the past three weeks, involving a total of 400 businesses. President Roosevelt revised the coal mining industry regulations so that he could appoint his own committee to monitor the behavior of the bituminous coal industry. This new industry regulation involves 95% of the American bituminous coal industry and approximately 400,000 miners.

Cuba's New President Strives for Stability 93

Receiving Strong Support from Student Factions

General Election Scheduled for Next Spring

Havana - The opposition party, during a meeting with President San Martin's government, presented President San Martin with an ultimatum, demanding his resignation to form a cabinet composed of representatives from all parties. San Martin replied, "I must wait for a qualified body to request my resignation before I can resign. In short, as long as the revolutionary agenda is implemented, who is president is not of much importance." Students leaning towards the revolutionary faction expressed their stance, saying, "San Martin cannot resign; at the very least, we should ask him not to resign, as his presidential authority was granted by us." It is widely believed that if San Martin allows himself to resign, the students will decide to retaliate against him, as they would view San Martin's resignation as a betrayal of the revolution. As for the soldiers, they are also gradually feeling deceived, as the soldiers' mutiny aimed only at improving their material treatment, but now the scope has expanded, and they are being implicated. (Havas dispatch, 19th)

Havana - Tonight, the Cuban cabinet resolved to hold a general election on April 1st of next year. Simultaneously, representatives for a constitutional convention will be elected, and the constitutional convention will be convened on May 20th to revise the new constitution.

Cuban politics are showing a clear trend towards radicalism. Although the government denies this, according to reliable American sources, in many places within the country, students and soldiers are not only attempting to exercise political affairs but also seeking to manage factories and the sugar industry. This news comes from provinces such as Sancti Spiritus and Camagüey. It is also reported that students and strikers in the town of Mayabeque have established a Soviet government and taken over sugar mills. However, a government spokesman said that this claim is highly doubtful. Cabinet members are currently drafting financial plans. President Grau San Martin promises to consolidate finances and stabilize the economy as soon as possible, adding that if there is no interference, the government can immediately restore industry and work throughout the island. The opposition party has not made any statements today. Several sources believe that the opposition leaders have agreed to temporary cooperation. In Havana, the number of workers returning to work is increasing daily. In Pinar del Río province, where a rebellion occurred last week, peace and tranquility are also reported. However, the San Martin government is currently still unwilling to cooperate with the United States on all issues, seeking to force the United States into de facto recognition. The U.S. government wants American sugar companies and Cuban sugar producers to agree on the allocation of the American market as soon as possible. The U.S. Department of Agriculture has notified the Cuban government, stating that the U.S. government still maintains that the amount of sugar Cuba sells in the U.S. should be equivalent to that sold by American farmers. However, it seems that the Cuban sugar industry currently lacks a central figure who can take responsibility for negotiations. Therefore, all negotiations on quotas and export limits are temporarily suspended. (National Telegram, 17th)

German-Austrian Peace Terms 94

Vienna, Havas, 19th - According to the "Neue Wiener Journal," Rosenberg, director of the foreign affairs office of the German National Socialist Party, has proposed the following conditions for "German-Austrian reconciliation" and the restoration of normal relations: (1) Austria should adopt the same diplomatic government as Germany. (2) Austria should support Germany in the League of Nations. (3) Austria should obtain Germany's consent before entering into economic agreements with other countries. (4) The policies pursued by Germany and Austria in Central Europe should be jointly determined by both countries. (5) The Austrian government should adopt an authoritative policy within the country that is compatible with German policies. Austrian newspapers should also cease anti-German propaganda. (6) The order prohibiting the Austrian National Socialist Party should be revoked. (7) Austrian National Socialists should be granted amnesty. (8) Austrian National Socialists who have been deprived of their citizenship should have their citizenship restored. (9) Austrian National Socialists who have fled to Germany and had their property confiscated should have it returned. (10) The Austrian government should prohibit all Marxist activities. (11) Germans who have fled into Austrian territory should be extradited. (12) Austria should emulate Germany in carrying out anti-Jewish movements and adopt "quota clauses" (i.e., the number of Jews in certain professions is subject to certain restrictions). (13) Austria should engage in close economic cooperation with Germany on a reciprocal basis. (14) The exit tax of one thousand marks levied on Germans entering German territory should be abolished. (15) Germany approves of Dollfuss as the Austrian Chancellor. (16) The Austrian Patriotic Front may continue to exist, but its political program should be revised. (17) Germany recognizes Austria's complete independence. The above conditions seem to have been given by Rosenberg to a key figure in the Austrian Farmers' Union, entrusted to him for delivery. After reviewing these conditions, this key figure seems to have presented a counter-proposal, accepting some of the conditions while rejecting others as interfering in Austrian internal affairs. It is also reported that German Foreign Minister Neurath declared that the conditions proposed by Rosenberg were not diplomatic and did not fully take into account the actual situation. He believed that the above conditions should be revised as follows: (1) Germany and Austria should cooperate sincerely in foreign policy and foreign trade. (2) Austrian domestic policy should adopt German policy to the extent that it does not overstep boundaries. (3) The solution to the Austrian National Socialist Party issue should be to detach the party from German influence. As for the Austrian Farmers' Union, it has issued a public statement rejecting the receipt of such proposals and refusing to discuss the above conditions. The statement also stated that the conditions proposed by Rosenberg are more difficult to accept today than in the past, which goes without saying.

Jin-Sui Army Implements Third Reorganization 95

The Reorganization Committee Sets Total Review

Taiyuan Correspondence - After Yan Xishan assumed the post of Pacification Director of Jin and Sui, he determined that the economies of Jin and Sui provinces were bankrupt, their vitality was over-injured, and the various military and administrative expenses were insufficient to cover expenditures, resulting in a significant annual deficit. In particular, military spending was the largest drain. Therefore, he decided to reduce the army to make up for the shortfall. In the past year or so, it has already been reorganized twice. According to current statistics, the finances of the two provinces are still short 140,000 to 150,000 yuan per month. Yan and the military leaders negotiated and decided to implement a third reorganization. The general plan has been drafted. The Jin-Sui Military Reorganization Committee held a meeting the other day to decide on the review methods for the armies in the two provinces. The attendees included Acting Chairman Yang Aiyuan, committee members Sun Chu, Zhou Dai, Zhu Shuguang, Kong Fan, Zhang Hanjie, Xie Lian, Chu Xichun, Wu Cui, Li Fangchi, Xu Heting, Ma Entian, and Chi Mingtu. It is reported that the committee, in order to ensure consistent performance assessment of the various units, divided the review into groups according to subject matter and sent specialists to conduct a detailed review. The decided key items are as follows: (1) Review dates: infantry review to begin on October 15th, cavalry and artillery review to begin on November 1st. (2) Review subjects: divided into academic, technical (parade, technology, combat, training, marching, work implementation, night exercises), and internal affairs (recognition of subordinates, own duties, military discipline) three items. (3) Number of review groups: a total of four groups. The first group will review the parade, technology, internal affairs, and academic subjects of the infantry, cavalry, and artillery, limited to one day per regiment, to be completed within three months. The second group will review the combat training, marching, work implementation, and night exercises of the infantry, limited to one day per regiment, to be completed within two and a half months. The third group will review the academic, marching, combat training, work implementation, and night exercises of the cavalry, limited to two days per regiment, to be completed within 25 days. The fourth group will review the academic, marching, combat training, work implementation, and night exercises of the artillery, limited to two days per regiment, to be completed within one month. (5) Chief Personnel: The chief of the first infantry review group is Lieutenant General Chu Xichun, the chief of the second infantry review group is Major General Li Fangchi, the chief of the third cavalry review group is Lieutenant General Huang Lucha, and the chief of the fourth artillery review group is Major General Ma Entian. All review committee members will be selected by the committee staff. Any changes to this year's review plan compared to last year have been notified by the committee to the various units by telegram for preparation. (September 16th)

Henan Bandits Capture Luyi 96

County Magistrate Xu Xizhi Kidnapped by Bandits

Provincial Government Sends Troops to Rescue and Recapture

Kaifeng Correspondence - Henan Province is known throughout the country for its bandits. In recent years, the Communists have risen in Shangqiu and Hankou, and the so-called eight counties of the Special Zone have become their sphere of influence. Bandits in other counties are also extremely rampant, such as Wang You, Li Changyou in western Henan, Xiao Liushao, Gu Dashen in Nanyang, Yang Xiaohei in Runan, Cheng Daorong in Huaiyang, and Du Jing in northern Henan. The larger groups have over 10,000 men, while the smaller groups have 500 to 600. However, Du Jing's group only harasses the borders of Anyang, Linzhang, and Neihuang counties and does not dare to go far. Wang, Li, Xiao, Gu, Yang, and Cheng's groups sometimes combine and sometimes separate, roaming south of the Yellow River. They have been repeatedly pursued and suppressed by government troops, but have never been eliminated. In the past three months, Xiao, Gu, Yang, Cheng's groups have mixed together, causing harm in the Runan and Xincai areas. Liu Zhi personally supervised the suppression once, and then commissioned the 52nd Division, the 1st Cavalry Brigade, the 13th Cavalry Brigade, and the Security Detachment Commander Cheng Ziyi's troops to be specifically responsible for the encirclement and suppression. After repeated attacks by the various units, the bandits dispersed and fled. Yang Xiaohei, Cheng Daorong, Huo Guodong, and other groups numbering several thousand, who were disturbing Huaiyang and Shenqiu, were relatively strong. On the 12th, they fled from the border of Huaiyang and Shenqiu counties and attempted to attack the county town of Luyi. At that time, the newly appointed County Magistrate Xu Xizhi sent two security teams to intercept them in different directions. However, due to the small number of soldiers and the large number of bandits, that night the bandits suddenly turned from the west to the south and directly approached the county town. At that time, there was only one security company stationed in the city, and the military strength was isolated and difficult to defend. However, Xu had served as the chief of the staff section of the headquarters of the three provinces for a long time and had considerable combat experience. He resolutely led a small number of troops to defend the county town of about nine li, braving arrows and charging, for a whole night. The next day, (13th) in the morning, the bandits used ladders to climb directly up the south gate in an attempt to seize the pass. At that time, Xu's troops, although their ammunition was exhausted, continued with knives and ordered the third section chief of the county government, Zou Jianbai, to direct the defense at the west gate. The bandits were repelled several times. Later, the bandits, unable to succeed, set fires on all sides and launched a fierce attack, and the west gate of the county was first captured at Yinke (3-5 AM) that morning. Xu was also kidnapped while leading his troops in street fighting. The former County Magistrate Zhong Shiming, who was staying in the county because his handover had not been completed, also fled in panic that day and disappeared. Trial Officers Wang Hanguang and Wang Shiying fled for their lives. Wang Hanguang was anxious and timid and fell off the city wall and was injured. He has now been moved to Haozhou for treatment. Wang Shiying hid in the city and was fortunate to escape harm. Zou Jianbai, the third section chief of the county government, rushed to Haozhou for help and sent telegrams appealing for assistance. Upon receiving the report, the provincial government sent the 14th Cavalry Brigade and the 2nd Security Regiment, and the 5th Company of the 7th District Security, to rush to assist in the suppression at night. The bandits, hearing the news, kidnapped County Magistrate Xu Xizhi on the morning of the 14th and fled far to the northeast. (At the moment, Zhen Jiyin, the commissioner of the 7th District, has personally gone to the county to handle the aftermath. Trial Officer Wang Shiying, who was hiding in the county town, has been pushed as the temporary county magistrate to maintain the status quo. The provincial government has ordered Zou Jianbai, the third section chief of the county, to return to the city immediately to temporarily serve as the county magistrate. The gist of the letter from the section chief to the provincial government is attached below (Cheng and Yang's bandit gangs, after being severely suppressed by Commander Cheng Ziyi, fled in two groups to disturb Huaiyang, Shenqiu, and other counties. The group that fled to Shenqiu repeatedly harassed Baimayi in Luyi County. County Magistrate Xu sent two security teams to intercept them several times. The bandits, unable to succeed in their attack, set fires everywhere and took the opportunity to seize the pass. Due to the disparity in numbers, the west gate was first captured at Yinke (3-5 AM) on the 13th. County Magistrate Xu was captured while leading his troops in street fighting. On the 14th, the bandits withdrew, and the county magistrate's life and death are unknown). (16th)

Bandit Atmosphere Still Rampant in Northern Anhui 97

Fuyang County Once in Danger

Bengbu Correspondence - Cheng Yaode's defeated troops from Henan Province previously fled into Fuyang in northern Anhui and mixed with the accumulated bandits Zhang Xueliang, Fan Ba, Jiang Ma, Lang Zepu, Huo Laohu (Guodong), and other gangs. They were numerous and harassed everywhere, burning, killing, raping, and plundering, extremely cruel. Later, the 3rd Army Commander Wang Jun supervised his troops and the Henan-Anhui armies to launch a large-scale joint suppression, which dispersed the bandit gangs. The remnant bandits fled to the territory of Taihe County, and were pursued by government troops, turning east and attempting to harass Wo and Meng. Just as they arrived at the Wo River, they were again met with a head-on attack by government troops and local militias. The bandits fled back to the west and lingered in the Shuangmiaoji and Cihepu areas at the junction of Fuyang and Taihe. Cheng Ziyi's Security Detachment from Henan Province, the 1st Regiment of the Anhui Provincial Security Team led by Zu Xinzai, and the 2nd Regiment led by Ni Rongxian, separately suppressed them. 3rd Army Commander Wang Jun then returned to Bengbu and stationed there. When Cheng Yaode and other bandit gangs were lingering in Cihepu and Shuangmiaoji, Cheng Ziyi led three regiments to suppress them. The bandits stubbornly resisted, engaging in fierce hand-to-hand combat for a day and a night. Both sides suffered casualties. The bandits finally could not hold out and fled west. When the bandits fled to about four or five li west of Fuyang City, they showed signs of attacking the city. The city gates were tightly closed, and the county town was in danger. The residents were extremely panicked. Fortunately, the local militia blocked them, and government troops arrived in pursuit. The bandits then fled through Baimiaoji to the Tianpengji area. Fuyang City was spared. However, the residents had already suffered a great fright. The city gates were only opened on the 14th. The bandits Xiao, Gu, Li Xiuling, and other gangs, who had disturbed Songji in the 7th district of Fuyang, were surrounded by Peng Yu's two cavalry brigades on three sides. The bandits desperately resisted and broke through the encirclement in the middle of the night, fleeing to Shenqiuji (120 li from Fuyang). Government troops are currently in pursuit. It is reported that there are more than 3,000 bandits with 2,000 guns. According to visitors from Shouxian, the notorious bandit Zhang Dabizi's gang in northern Anhui, after capturing Hanshan County and plundering it, fled to the Zhujiawan and Zhangjiaqiao areas at the junction of Shou and Dingyuan, burning, killing, raping, and plundering, and were extremely brutal. Everywhere they passed, all houses were empty. The county's security team has joined forces with the 2nd and 3rd district teams of Dingyuan to encircle and suppress the bandits. Jiang Yi, the chief of the Changhuai River Water Police Bureau, had previously returned to Bengbu by ship with his team because the bandit situation in the Fuyang and Ying areas had dispersed. However, the bandits returned, and Fuyang was in a tight spot. Only staying in Bengbu and Suzhou, he returned to the Fuyang and Ying areas to defend. (September 18th)

Shanghai Group Representatives Present Banner to Su Bingwen 98

Held in Suzhou

Suzhou Correspondence - Representatives of various groups in Shanghai, Ye Jiaxing, Wang Honghui, Sun Mingqi, etc., held a banner presentation ceremony to General Su Bingwen at the Garden Hotel. The situation was tragic and is recorded in detail as follows:

The meeting opened at 11:30 a.m. on the 19th. Attendees included representatives from all walks of life: the county government, the Public Security Bureau, the Education Bureau, the Third District Administrative Inspectorate, the Party Headquarters, the Farmers' Association, the High Court, the Reformatory, and local figures Zhang Yunbo, Fei Zhongshen, and Yang Yongqing, president of Soochow University. Wang Honghui, Ye Jiaxing, and Sun Mingqi were publicly elected as the presidium. After the music played and the meeting began, Ye Jiaxing first reported on the significance of the banner presentation. Amid applause, the embroidered banner with the four characters "Anti-Japanese Hero" was presented to Mr. Su. Next, gold medals were presented. There were four other gold medals, which were presented to Zhang Dianjiu, Gao Junling, Wu Delin, and Wang Erzhan, and accepted on their behalf by Mr. Su's entourage. Next, Mr. Su delivered a thank-you speech, roughly saying that at the time of resisting the stubborn enemy, he had intended to destroy the puppet organization, but as a result, he ran out of ammunition and food, was deeply oppressed by the enemy army, and retreated to the Russian border, failing to recover the lost territory. He was deeply ashamed. Now, he only had his original intention, continued to work hard, and prepared to use his life to fight the enemy in the future. Next, Zhang Yunbo gave a speech, roughly saying that the Chinese people are now like people who have swallowed sleeping pills, sleeping for 733 days. Although they have awareness in their hearts, because they are bound, they have very little action. Only a few people can show admirable behavior. Such people are indeed heroes, but national affairs cannot be supported by a few heroes. He hoped that everyone would stand up and help this hero save the country, otherwise it would be difficult to support him alone, and it would be a pity to bury this hero. Next, Yang Yongqing, the president of Soochow University, gave a speech, roughly divided into three points: (1) Gold medals and flags are good, but they do not have the permanent admiration of all human beings in the world. The admiration of human beings is better than flags. (2) This time, the compatriots in Shanghai came to Suzhou to present the flag, seemingly representing the people of Suzhou, because the people of Suzhou also have this intention. The so-called worship of heroes, for all ages, is the same in heart. (3) From now on, we should think about how we can be worthy of national heroes. Next, Zhu Jiaji, a standing committee member of the Party Headquarters, gave a speech, roughly saying that there is more than one way to resist Japan, indirect and direct, with different means, such as merchants resisting goods, academic circles promoting, etc. Therefore, we should all take on the responsibility of resisting Japan and saving the country. Finally, a representative from the High Court gave a speech, wishing General Su victory after receiving the banner, and that the gold medal would make China golden and brilliant. Then, a group photo was taken and the meeting adjourned.

Songjiang Hit by Hurricane 99

The Loss of Property

Yesterday (18th) it rained at dawn. At 2 p.m., a hurricane suddenly struck, more violent than last month. Waterway traffic was temporarily suspended. The tide rose sharply, almost level with the shore. Countless thatched houses and car sheds in the suburbs were blown over. Telephone lines were disrupted, hindering communication. Electric lights flickered, all of which were beyond human control. Late rice is the main agricultural product of this county. It is now the flowering season for late rice. After a day and night of hurricane ravaging, there is no hope for a bumper harvest this year. The loss is incalculable. Old farmers, who work hard all year round, were saddened by this setback. The hurricane stopped at about 1 p.m. today (19th).

Suzhou - Liu Jingdu Commits Suicide Out of Disgust with the World 101

On the 19th of the Inter-Railway Hotel, a traveler committed suicide, leaving a suicide note. The guest wrote his name as Liu Jingdu, about 30 years old. He arrived in Suzhou from Beijing on the 18th, wearing a serge Chinese suit with the clothes inside out, with the character "Cheng" on them. This morning (19th), he was found to have taken poison and was immediately sent to Suyong Hospital, but he died before he could be treated. The suicide note was very long and spoke of national affairs. The main points were: (1) The 918 anniversary has been two weeks, and I don't know how many slogans have been changed, and I don't know how many meetings have been held, but not an inch of lost land has been recovered, and the Japanese army is now threatening Zhangjiakou again. The people of Yuguan are following the pseudo-Manchuria. In this situation, what hope is there other than national subjugation? (2) The big shots are always one step behind. When France occupied the Nine Islands, we slowly investigated after they declared it, and then protested. (3) The Japanese army has built a great garrison in Shanghai, but I have not heard of any expression from the government. (4) Apart from the written publicity in the news media and the patterned commemorative meetings of the Party Headquarters, what other expressions are there in Beijing, Shanghai, and Suzhou for the 918 national humiliation? The people have long forgotten the pain of the loss of the Northeast. Today (probably referring to the 18th), apart from the old sky still crying, the air is as silent as if it were dead. (5) I am a weak person, and my death is not a pity, but my death cannot rest in peace, that is, when will the Japanese slaves be rampant, and then can I go to kill them in Fusang? This kind of evil society is showing signs of national subjugation everywhere. There are no Japanese goods anywhere, sad, sad. The first hatred is for corrupt officials who prey on the people. If I have knowledge underground, I will definitely become a fierce ghost and kill them, to relieve my accumulated hatred. (6) The rural economy in the country is bankrupt, and we still have to bring in a lot of cotton and wheat from foreign countries to compete with the farmers in the market. The Supervisory Yuan is equal to a dummy. (7) Which province does not have bandits, Hubei, Jiangxi, Hunan, Sichuan, Anhui? The government troops have fought for four or five years, and it is still like this. I am unwilling to be a subjugated slave, so I commit suicide, etc.

Wuxi - The Rice Industry Discount Dispute Resolved 102

The rice and bean industry discount dispute, which has been going on for several months, was mediated by the Suzhou rice tycoon, Mr. Zhou Hongqing. However, due to the insistence of both parties, the mediation once broke down. Therefore, Mr. Zhou expressed dissatisfaction with both parties. Zhao Zixin, the chairman of the local rice industry association, even expressed his resignation. Public sentiment generally blamed the Sanliqiao segment, while the six dissenting firms, seeing the situation was not good, resolutely sought peace. There are two reasons: (1) If they oppose to the end, they will become the target of public criticism from their peers, and there will be no way to clean up the situation. (2) Although they have been advocating a 9.9 discount for several months, their business has not increased. Moreover, it is now the season for new grains to be harvested, and if they do not resolve the issue as soon as possible, it will certainly affect their own vital interests. Therefore, representatives of both parties gathered at the Longmao Rice Store yesterday to make a final mediation. Mr. Zhou announced the mediation method, deciding to implement the new 9.84 discount system together from October 1st. Both parties expressed their approval. Once the county chamber of commerce approves it, the entire matter can be resolved.

Abominable Teahouse Attendant Attempts to Rape Female Guest 103

The New World Hotel, under the Gongyun Bridge in the county, recently received Shao, a traveler from Yixing, and his wife, Xu Shuyuan. Shao worked as a recorder in the Shanghai Special District Court. This time, he was going to Shanghai after his honeymoon, and Xu Shuyuan, feeling deeply attached, sent him off to Wuxi. They talked long into the night and did not sleep until the east turned white and the rooster crowed. Shao hurriedly bid farewell to his wife and took the train to Shanghai. Shuyuan, having not closed her eyes all night, fell into a hazy sleep. Suddenly, a teahouse attendant, Gai Xinggen, opened the door and entered, kneeling on both knees before Shuyuan, begging for pleasure. Shuyuan was startled and shouted. The teahouse attendant then fled out of the room. Later, Shuyuan called her husband's younger brother, Shao Xiaobao, a staff member of the experimental department of the Provincial Education Institute at the Sheqiaotou, who arrived and dragged the accountant Liu Zhiqing, Xu Zhisheng, and the teahouse attendant Gai Xinggen to the Public Security Second Sub-bureau, who transferred them to the County Public Security Bureau. The Third Section interrogated them and sentenced the teahouse attendant to seven days of detention for his improper behavior, as a warning. Liu Zhiqing and others were ordered to return together. However, the plaintiff will formally file a lawsuit in court based on the crime of attempted rape under the Criminal Law and request the Public Security Bureau to explain the legal basis for sentencing attempted rape to only seven days of detention, in order to maintain law and order.

Changzhou: Silk Firm Employee Rapes Young Woman 104

Yongtaichang Silk Firm, located in Lijiabridge Town, Wuyi County, recently hired Yuan Huaimin from Wuxi to purchase autumn cocoons. Gu Jizhen, a 17-year-old woman from the town, possessed remarkable beauty, and Yuan repeatedly harbored lascivious intentions towards her. Gu persistently rejected his advances. On the 17th, Jizhen traveled by boat to visit relatives in the city. Yuan followed her to the city. That afternoon, Jizhen intended to return to the town on the same boat, but Yuan followed her onto the boat and forcibly made her disembark. He suggested that he accompany her to visit his girlfriend, Cao Fenghuan, in Dasuo Lane. Jizhen, unable to shake him off, hired a carriage to Dasuo Lane. By the time she returned to the pier, the boat had already departed. At this point, Yuan deployed his seductive tactics and coerced her into going to the Large Guesthouse in the western suburbs, booking room number 15. He prevented her from leaving. That night, he forcibly raped her. The next morning, Jizhen's grandmother, Madam Yin, arrived in the city, searching for her granddaughter in vain. She enlisted the help of others to search everywhere. Eventually, they found her at the guesthouse in the western suburbs, where Jizhen was weeping bitterly in bed. Upon inquiring about the situation, Jizhen recounted the entire ordeal. Yuan, however, had already left early in the morning. Madam Yin, filled with uncontrollable rage, enlisted others to track down Yuan. They apprehended him in front of the County Government. On the afternoon of the 18th, he was escorted to the County Court Prosecutor's Office. Prosecutor Guan Junjie conducted the interrogation, during which Yuan recounted the details of the incident. Prosecutor Guan determined that Yuan Huaimin had intentionally seduced a young woman and forcibly raped her, which was truly detestable. He ordered that Yuan be shackled and imprisoned, pending prosecution under the law.

Taicang: Old Woman Returns Lost Money 105

Xin Yongshun Flower Firm in Jiuqu Town, under the jurisdiction of the county, sent an apprentice named Xiao Bingsheng on the 17th by bicycle to Shenxin Flower Store in Fuqiao Town to collect 1,000 yuan in funds. The apprentice took the receipt to collect the money. After counting the banknotes, he wrapped them in paper and placed them in his short shirt pocket, then rode the bicycle back to the firm. Unexpectedly, along the way, due to the violent vibrations of the bicycle, the banknotes fell out of his pocket onto the road. An elderly woman found them and, upon inspecting the package, saw that it contained a large amount of money. She sat by the roadside, waiting for the owner to claim them. When the apprentice arrived at the firm and attempted to hand over the money to the owner, he found his pocket empty. He was immediately shocked and frantic. He rushed back along the same route in search of the money. Along the way, the elderly woman saw his distressed state and asked him what was wrong. The apprentice told her the truth. The elderly woman returned all the banknotes to him without missing a single one. Such an elderly woman is truly worthy of admiration!

Jiashan: Suicide Due to Economic Pressure 106

Quan Qixin, the young owner of Xinji Bookstore in the county town, was by nature timid and kind. He diligently managed the store every day, never straying far. However, due to the declining business, he faced extreme economic pressure. After much deliberation, he decided to seek a way out elsewhere. In June of this year, he went to Zhenjiang to find work. Despite his efforts, he found no opportunities, and his pockets were empty. Driven to desperation and at wit's end, he secretly ingested sodium nitrite and took his own life. When Quan's family learned of this news, they were shocked and immediately rushed to Zhenjiang to bring his remains back to their hometown.

Kidnappers Resort to Cruel Torture After Failed Ransom Demand 107

Shen Hesheng and his son Linsheng from Dayao Township in this county were kidnapped by the bandit leader Shitou Xiaodi, who demanded a ransom of 30,000 yuan, to be paid by a set date at the Hangzhou Railway Station. The Shen family, being of moderate means, could not afford such a large sum. As a result, they delayed the payment. Unexpectedly, the gang of bandits, believing that the Shen family had no intention of paying the ransom, subjected Shen Hesheng and his son, along with other kidnap victims from the Suzhou area, to cruel torture in the area north of Dingpeng and Beitangtan. They applied strips of cloth all over their backs, then coated them with raw lacquer. After the lacquer had partially dried, they ripped off one end of the cloth, tearing the skin with it, causing excruciating pain. Their agonizing cries for help were unbearable to hear. Residents in the area witnessed this and, feeling deeply sorry for them, reported the horrific scene to the Shen family, urging them to pay the ransom immediately, or else they feared that the victims would not survive. The cruelty of the bandits' methods is truly shocking.

Hangzhou: Two Bandits Executed by Firing Squad by the Court 108

Qi Xiaoseng, also known as Qi Changde, a native of Henan, residing in Caotang, Pingyao County, Hangzhou, was a notorious bandit with a long history of crimes. He had repeatedly evaded capture. On November 4th of last year, he and eight other bandits, including the Huzhou bandit leader Hu Qiufa, carrying firearms, went to Hechitou at around 9 PM and kidnapped Ruan Jinfang and others. Ruan Jinfang's family immediately reported the incident to the local militia police, who launched a search. The local standing militia encountered the bandits in Huawan Tumen and exchanged fire. During the battle, Qi Xiaoseng was shot in the upper right ribs, and Hu Qiufa was shot in the right leg. Militia soldier Wang Xiandu was also injured. Ruan Jinfang, the kidnapped victim, took the opportunity to flee and escape unharmed during the fighting. The wounded bandits, Qi Xiaoseng and Hu Qiufa, were taken by their accomplices to Xujiacun and hidden in the home of Zhang the Monk. The next day, the militia police followed the trail of blood to Zhang the Monk's house and arrested Qi Xiaoseng and Hu Chunfa. They were escorted to the Provincial Garrison Headquarters and then transferred to the Court Prosecutor's Office. After investigation, the prosecutor determined that Qi Xiaoseng and Hu Qiufa were guilty of violating Article 1, Section 1 of the Provisional Regulations for the Punishment of Bandits. He filed a public prosecution and requested approval from the Provincial Government. The Provincial Government approved the execution by firing squad. At 8 AM yesterday morning, they were taken from the detention center, their identities were verified, and they were escorted outside Qingbo Gate for execution by firing squad.

Letter to the Editor 109

To the esteemed Editor:

On the 18th of this month, your newspaper's Suzhou local news column published a report concerning an accusation. We have investigated that, in July, the report of a Liuhe anti-smuggling officer named Wang Fengzhang, et al., crossing the border to arrest people and disrupting public order, prompted our office to issue orders for their apprehension. In August, on multiple days, Wang Fengzhang, et al., again, in civilian clothes and armed, crossed the border at night to arbitrarily harass people, causing merchants and residents to flee in alarm and nearly causing an incident. Consequently, the Public Security Sub-Bureau's police team took Wang Fengzhang, et al., into custody and brought them in for questioning. Subsequently, a formal letter was received from the Jiangsu Provincial Narcotics Suppression Bureau, stating that the officer's rash actions were inappropriate. The bureau issued an order to its sub-bureau to reprimand the officer and authorized the bureau to send personnel to take him back for handling. Wang Fengzhang, however, showed no remorse and acted unlawfully. In addition to submitting a report to the province for strict investigation, we request that your publication make a correction. Thank you for your attention.

Kunshan County Government, September 19th.

Local News

Typhoon Passed Shanghai Yesterday; Taibao Songjiang Seawall in Danger Yesterday Morning 110

Officials and Merchants Telegraph Requests for Funds for Emergency Repairs

Various Areas Severely Affected by Typhoon, Suffering Losses

Yesterday, the Weather Cleared, but Shipping Remains Obstructed

Another Typhoon Fortunately Dissipated

The second typhoon passed Dajishan in the early hours of yesterday morning, moving towards the southwest corner of Korea. When it passed Shanghai, the tides surged dramatically, disrupting transportation and causing vegetable prices to skyrocket. The Baoshan seawall was severely battered by the waves, collapsing in five places, totaling over 200 zhang in length. The seawall repair projects in Wusong Wumufeng and other locations were completely washed away by the waves, with several sections of the earthen dam collapsing. Many cotton and rice fields were flooded. The Municipal Chamber of Commerce and the Baoshan County Government telegraphed the Municipal and Provincial Governments, requesting funds for emergency repairs. Details are as follows:

Yesterday's Observatory Report: Passed Dajishan Observatory 111

The Observatory reported that the typhoon struck the coast of Zhejiang on the afternoon of the previous day, heading north-northwest, threatening to make landfall in Wenzhou Bay and circle inland to strike Shanghai from behind. However, the direction changed in the evening, and at approximately 9 PM, it reached the sea east of Ningbo, moving north-north-east. By 2:30 AM yesterday morning, it had passed Dajishan, outside the mouth of Wusong, only 60-70 English miles from Shanghai. This was west of Huawushan, which the previous typhoon had passed. Although Shanghai was not hit by the center of the typhoon yesterday morning, it was affected by its periphery.

Moving towards Korea The Observatory issued its first report at 10 AM yesterday, stating that the air pressure in Korea and the Sea of Japan had increased. The typhoon scoured the East China Sea, passing east of Shanghai (i.e., Dajishan) at 2:30 AM yesterday, heading north-north-east. At 6 AM yesterday, it was at 32 degrees north latitude and 123 degrees east longitude (approximately 90 English miles northeast of Shanghai) in the ocean, with astonishingly strong winds. By 2 PM, it had reached 33 degrees north latitude and 124 degrees east longitude, moving north-north-east. This location is approximately 150 English miles northeast of Shanghai and is tilting further northeast, heading towards the southwest corner of the Korean Peninsula. As a result, the southwest coast of Korea is covered with storm clouds, and the tides in the Korean Strait will rise. The wind force along the coast of Zhejiang has decreased.

Liaison ship cut off Japan United News Agency, Shimonoseki, 19th telegram said: Shimonoseki and the Korean Strait area, on the 19th, were hit by a typhoon, with great force. At 6 AM, the wind speed was 12 meters. The Korean liaison ships that departed from the local area at 10:30 AM were all withdrawn midway. On the other hand, the ship sailing from Busan to Shimonoseki was also not seen. The contact between the two places was completely cut off.

Another Typhoon According to the Observatory's report, the second typhoon (referring to the typhoon that was proceeding due north at 23 degrees north latitude and 123 degrees east longitude southeast of Taiwan at 2 PM the previous day) was gradually dissipating after reaching southeast Taiwan from northern Luzon, due to the circulation and attraction of the first typhoon (referring to the one that passed Dajishan yesterday morning). Otherwise, at 6 AM yesterday morning, it would have reached approximately 120 English miles southeast of Wenzhou, at 27 degrees north latitude and 123 degrees east longitude, striking Shanghai again. A second disaster was fortunately avoided.

Damage to the Songjiang Seawall 112

A reporter from New Voice News Agency heard yesterday that many sections of the Wusong Baoshan seawall were in danger, so he took a car to investigate. He inspected the situation at the Hanchuan Pier, the Public Garden, Tanjiaham, Aomufeng (Lion Bridge), also known as Shitang, and the Baoshan Xuejiatan, Gujiadun, and Zhangjiazha areas. The details obtained are recorded below:

Waves on the Customs Wharf (Photo by Qichang) 113

Wusong Road Starting from the northern section of Jungong Road, the paddy fields near the coast were completely flooded. North of Wuquan Road, the area around the Zhabei Power Plant (behind Shanghai University) was a vast expanse of water, turning into a swamp. The thatched huts built near the coast were half-submerged in water, and residents were frantically carrying items out of their homes and retrieving objects from the water. The terrain along the Zhanghuaham and Yunzaobang sections was particularly low, and the water had flooded the Songhu Railway tracks. Therefore, yesterday the Songhu train only ran to Zhanghuaham. In addition, along the road, more than ten trees and utility poles were broken by the wind.

Capsized Boats in Wusong After arriving at Wusong Town, the embankment along the Waimala Road was eroded by the tide, and the soil had collapsed. A utility pole had fallen there. After 1 AM yesterday morning, the streets of the town were also flooded by the rising tide, and the streets were filled with water. When the typhoon passed, the houses near the coast shook, and tiles flew everywhere. After 9 AM, the telephone and electric lights were cut off and extinguished due to the broken poles, plunging the area into darkness. On the river, one ship transporting pigs and one jellyfish boat were overturned by the wind and tide. The extent of the losses is still under investigation. Fortunately, the people on board were rescued, and no lives were lost.

Collapse of Stone Embankment As the reporter continued to inspect the various locations, he found that the sections north of Yunzaobang along the Huangpu River from Wusong were damaged, including Hanchuan Pier, the Public Garden, Tanjiaham, Yangmatou, and Wumufeng (Lion Bridge). The Hanchuan Pier was originally an earthen dam, and half of it had collapsed due to the tidal water, which then flooded into the area. Two-thirds of Tanjiaham was gone. Yangmatou is near the Wusong Fortified Island. The terrain there is low, and the water caused extensive damage when it rushed in. The Aquatic Products School and the Merchant Marine School were flooded, with water reaching a height of more than ten feet. By noon yesterday, the water had still not receded. The most dangerous area was Wumufeng, also known as the Stone Embankment, which winds its way to Baoshan and is ten li long. There are thirteen layers of stone steps from the bottom to the top. Eight of them have been washed away, five in Baoshan and one in Wusong. This embankment was built during the Qing Dynasty, nearly a hundred years ago, by Hu Renji, the magistrate of Baoshan County at the time, who used his personal fortune and donations to build it. It was built because there had been a major flood, and after the embankment collapsed, the water reached as far as Wuxi. Its significance was paramount, so Hu Renji, with foresight, spared no expense to complete it. To this day, the people of Baoshan and Wusong still praise his name. After the warning of the impending typhoon reached Wusong the day before yesterday, Tang Chengzhong, a member of the municipal committee of the district, immediately hired 75 workers to fill sacks with soil and carry out emergency repairs. The work began at 9 AM and continued until 4 PM. However, this temporary work was completely destroyed between midnight and 1 AM, when the northeast wind and the tide came together. Therefore, yesterday morning, Committee Member Tang again led 75 workers, and temporarily recruited nearby villagers, to carry out repairs again. North of Yunzaobang, including Qieluting (formerly Jiangtang) and Sections 22 and 25 of the district, the terrain in Yangjiaham and Zoujiaqiao of Qieluting is the lowest. In places where the water was one foot deep, those two locations experienced depths of four to five feet. Therefore, at the height of the storm yesterday morning, the water depth was over five feet. Half of the houses were submerged in water, and by 10 AM yesterday morning, it was still about three feet deep. Sections 22 and 25 consist of two earthen dams. They were severely damaged during the previous typhoon, and yesterday morning's damage was even worse.

Rice and Cotton Submerged The areas near the two sections are all farmland, so the cotton and rice in the fields were only visible above the water like seedlings, a vast expanse of water. The water will only recede after the weather clears for several days. According to farmers who were inspecting the damage in the fields, if the water recedes quickly, the cotton harvest will be reduced by 60 percent. Part of the rice fields have already been harvested, so the situation is slightly better. Overall, the most dangerous period was from midnight to 1 AM the night before last until 2 AM yesterday morning. From 1 AM to 3 AM, the wind force decreased slightly, and the tide gradually receded. Although the wind force was very strong and the tide surged as before yesterday morning after 8 AM, the wind had shifted to the northwest, which was not as severe as the day before.

Urgent Need for Repairs According to Tang Chengzhong, a member of the municipal committee of the district, if the embankments in the Wusong area had been repaired promptly after the previous incident, the damage this time would not have been so severe. He repeatedly requested assistance from the Public Works Bureau to carry out emergency repairs to avoid further danger. However, because the typhoon came so suddenly, the Public Works Bureau had not yet sent anyone to repair the damage when the danger became apparent. The citizens of Wusong are now most concerned about the high tides on the third day of the eighth lunar month and are in a state of anxiety. Therefore, they have requested the Municipal Government to instruct the Public Works Bureau to send workers and materials to Wusong to carry out repairs as soon as possible. Today, the Public Works Bureau sent Technician Gu to inspect the situation once in the morning.

Baotang Washed Away Near the city of Baoshan County, the water had gradually receded yesterday. The telephone was cut off at 7 PM the night before last and had not been restored by last night. The lights also went out once at 7 PM, then came back on, but went out again at 10 PM, and it will be difficult to restore them for a while. All the new embankment projects that were repaired with the 30,000 yuan allocated by the Provincial Government after the previous incident were completely washed away by the strong winds, rainstorms, and tides at around 1 AM yesterday morning. All previous efforts were wasted. More than half of the 27 zhang wooden stakes were washed away, and the 3 zhang head was also about to be breached. Yesterday, workers were ordered to throw stones to block the breach. Five to six feet of the old stone surface were washed away. The stone cave area was not seriously affected. The area north of Beijiantou near the county seat was the most severely affected. Therefore, yesterday, the county magistrate of Baoshan County, Jin Qingzhang, in addition to telegraphing the Provincial Government to send personnel to inspect the situation and urgently requesting funds for repairs, also convened a meeting of various groups such as the Chamber of Commerce at 1 PM in the afternoon to discuss emergency blocking measures.

Situation in Liuhe The embankments in Liuhe were washed away by the seawater during the typhoon and rainstorm the night before last in two places: (1) Beidaotang Temple, a total of nine zhang were washed away; (2) Five Houses, a total of five zhang were washed away. Several houses were destroyed. Yesterday, patrolman Zhu Huanong and workers went to inspect and carry out emergency repairs. The damage was not very serious.

Current Status of Repairs In Wusong, the Municipal Public Works Bureau sent Xue Baokang and workers to carry out repairs once at 1 AM the night before last. However, due to the strong winds, raging tides, and difficult working conditions, the work was stopped after only about an hour. Yesterday morning, the Public Works Bureau sent Technician Gu to inspect again. It was originally planned to carry out repairs immediately, but as of 2 PM, the workers had not yet arrived in Wusong, so only the workers hired by the Wusong Municipal Committee continued to carry out repairs.

Water in front of Sincere Company on Nanjing Road (Photo by Qichang)

Tang Gong's high By the Municipal Works Bureau Section II Section Chief Xu Yu reporter, to Shanghai area of the seawall, the most important only for the high bridge aspect, because the place is located on the east bank of the Pujiang River, the appropriate location of the Yangtze River estuary, wind aggression, than any other place, especially the Shanghai since learning of the hurricane passage news, that is, prepared to grab repair and all the work. Railway Traffic Also Hindered - Shanghai-Hangzhou Situation - The Previous Night 116

During the hurricane and rainstorm, except for the Beijing-Shanghai Railway which was undamaged, the Shanghai-Hangzhou Railway, specifically the 414th freight train leaving Shanghai from the Zhakou station and traveling near Songjiang, experienced a severe event around 8 PM. The roofs of the freight cars numbered 1190 and 1214 were violently struck by the wind and rain, causing them to be blown off and scattered along the route. The incident was immediately reported by telegram to patrol workers and railway police along the line, who located the scattered debris. The damaged cars, after unloading their cargo at Shanghai Station at 9:30 PM, were sent to the Zhakou factory for repairs. Simultaneously, the telephone at the Rihuigang Station was damaged and short-circuited due to the storm, burning the telephone lines. Telephones at the South Station and the Xinlonghua Telephone Bureau were also disrupted by the storm. Fortunately, the telegraph and long-distance telephone lines throughout the network were undamaged and remained operational. However, between Songjiang and Shihudang along the Shanghai section, five or six telephone poles and roadside trees planted near the Shanghai stations were blown down, though the wires were not broken, allowing uninterrupted communication. The Railway Bureau has already dispatched workers to repair the damage.

Shanghai-Songhu Situation Yesterday - Due to the Zhanghuabang Railway Bridge on the Beijing-Shanghai Railway's Songhu branch line being submerged by floodwaters, trains yesterday could only run from the North Station to Zhanghuabang.

Ship Services Still Suspended Yesterday - Shanghai-Ningbo Still Suspended 117

The regular liners "New Beijing" and "New Ning Shao," which were canceled the day before due to the heavy wind, remained canceled yesterday even after the hurricane passed. Ning Shao Company initially planned to resume service with the "New Ning Shao," and sent personnel to Taikoo Company to inquire about the "New Beijing's" sailing status. After consultation, it was decided not to sail and instead resume scheduled services today. The Sanbei Company's "Ningxing" and China Merchants' "Xinming" were sheltering from the storm in Ningbo. Both companies sent telegrams to reschedule their arrival in Shanghai for today to avoid disrupting the schedule. Other Shanghai-Taiwan and Wenzhou liners were also delayed by one day each. China Merchants' "Jiahe" was sheltering from the storm outside Wusong and had not arrived, so its departure for Wenzhou was also postponed.

Post Shipments Postponed - The first-class British ship "Nardistan" was originally scheduled to leave yesterday, carrying 600 bales of Huzhou silk and over 4,000 chests of tea from Shanghai. Due to the heavy wind and rain the day before, the silk and tea could not be loaded without getting wet, forcing a one-day postponement. It is now scheduled to depart for England today. The Dollar Line's "President Cleveland," arriving in Shanghai from the United States, was originally scheduled to enter the port yesterday. However, it was struck by a hurricane 120 miles off the coast of Shanghai, forcing it to anchor outside Wusong for shelter. In the afternoon, the company received a telegram from the ship reporting no unexpected damage to the vessel, and it is scheduled to enter port at 8:30 AM today.

Three Ships Arrived Yesterday - Ships from Taikoo, Jardine Matheson, China Merchants, Nippon Yusen Kaisha, and others that were originally scheduled to arrive yesterday did not. But there were no messages of danger reported. Only two Yangtze River ships arrived in Shanghai yesterday: the China Merchants' "Jiang'an" and the Socony-Vacuum's "Meiping." The Dada's "Daiwa" also sailed to Shanghai from the Yangtze River, so they were safer. Only three Yangtze River ships departed; no ocean-going vessels sailed.

Rice Boats Capsized - During the violent hurricane and tidal surge the previous night, two rice boats, "Shen Zengfu" and "Wu Fuhai," anchored near Xuejiabang in Nanshi, were struck by the fierce winds and waves, snapping their mooring ropes. As a result, they could not be saved and capsized immediately. Fortunately, the two boats were close to a large sand barge, and the boat owners and their crews were rescued by the barge's crew, avoiding any casualties. However, the loss of the two boats was irreparable. The "Shen Zengfu" was loaded with 150 shi of low-quality rice for the Hengyiyuan Rice Store in Sijing, which was completely lost, estimated at over 1,000 yuan. The boat's planks and miscellaneous items were also worth 500 to 600 yuan. The "Wu Fuhai" was a self-selling boat, and although the rice was unloaded in time, it had already been loaded with engine oil and motors for various merchants in the interior, resulting in an estimated loss of around 1,000 yuan. The total loss for the two boats is estimated at around 4,000 yuan. While the hull of the "Shen Zengfu" boat remains, there is no trace of the "Wu Fuhai," causing the boat owners to weep uncontrollably. Japanese Ship Sends SOS - The Mitsui & Co. freighter "Taiei Maru," which was loading cargo in Shanghai for Dalian, was struck by a hurricane outside the Wusong port at 2 AM yesterday. In addition to dropping anchor, the captain ordered the entire crew to do their best to resist the storm and sent a telegram for assistance. The Ministry of Communications' Coastal Wireless Station received the message at 2 AM yesterday and immediately notified Mitsui & Co. At 3 AM, another telegram was received stating that the hurricane had passed, and the ship was safely out of danger and proceeding to Dalian as planned. Also, at 12:45 AM yesterday, the Coastal Wireless Station received an emergency call from the Japanese merchant ship "Hiknsth Maru," which encountered a hurricane at 31.27 degrees north latitude and 12.40 degrees east longitude. However, according to Mitsui & Co., the ship is not owned by them.

Huangpu River Traffic - All Yangtze and ocean-going vessels of Jardine Matheson, Taikoo, China Merchants, and Ning Shao were suspended because the customs had previously sounded warning cannons. As for the ships still in operation, the company also sent telegrams to tell them to stop. All Huangpu River ferries were also suspended due to high winds and waves, which caused inconvenience for passengers traveling back and forth. The municipal ferries on Dongmen Road and Dongchang Road were extremely crowded, and the Municipal Bureau of Public Works temporarily added one additional ferry yesterday morning.

Situation of Losses in Various Places - Collapsed Houses and Injured People - Inside the City 118

At 10:30 PM the previous night, the roof of Chu Fuqing's house on Tutang Street suddenly collapsed due to wind and rain, falling onto the roof of the east wing of the neighboring No. 5 Flour Industry Association. It collapsed instantly, injuring Xie Tangshi, a widow sleeping in the room, her young son Xie Yincai, and their housemate Mi Jinmei and Gao Ruiliang. The local First District Second Precinct sent police officers to rescue them. They were transported by car to Shanghai Hospital for treatment. Mi Jinmei suffered the most severe injuries to her head and waist. Xie Yincai and Gao Ruiliang both sustained minor head injuries and were kept in the hospital for observation. Also, the rear building of Lu Baosheng's house at No. 29, Lane 57, Sangyuan Street, outside Xiaonanmen in Nanshi, suddenly collapsed. Fortunately, no one was inside, and no one was injured. At around 9 PM, a short wall next to the kitchen of Dr. Hu Hongfang's house at No. 49, Xundao Street, inside Dadongmen, fell into the adjacent Tan Family Lane, but no one was injured. Over ten advertising boards belonging to the Public Works Bureau on the Republic Road were blown down by the wind.

Electrocution Deaths - Yesterday morning, around Xiaoximen, telephone lines and electricity lines crossed, causing a temporary communication outage. The Telephone Bureau received the report and dispatched craftsman Fei Jintao to repair it. Unexpectedly, the craftsman fell after being electrocuted. His skull was crushed by a stone, his brains splattered, and his limbs were severely injured. He was taken by police car to Shanghai Hospital for treatment, and then to Baolong Hospital. According to the doctors, his pulse was weak and erratic, and he was unconscious and still in critical condition. Without intervention, there was concern that he would not survive. Yesterday morning around 1 AM, Cao Baofu, a 49-year-old man from Taizhou, and his 14-year-old son Cao Xiaoyou, were sound asleep in their house on Guangfu Road in Caojiadu, west of Shanghai, when they were awakened by the sound of wind and rain. Suddenly, they heard a loud crash. The son ran out to investigate and was immediately electrocuted and fell to the ground when a broken power line fell. Cao Baofu saw his son injured and immediately jumped out to rescue him. However, he also stepped on the end of the wire and was severely electrocuted, immediately dying. His son was taken to the hospital for treatment and miraculously recovered. By yesterday afternoon, he had recovered and was sent home. The Sixth District was notified, and they ordered the local police to report to the court for inspection.

Broken Poles - During the second hurricane that struck Shanghai the previous night, the telephone lines of the Shanghai Telephone Bureau of the Ministry of Communications were severely damaged by the strong winds and rain, especially in Longhua and Zhenru. The three districts of Zhabei, Nanshi, and Pudong were less affected.

Two telephone poles were blown down in Wusong and workers were dispatched yesterday morning at 7 AM to repair them. The repairs were completed by yesterday afternoon. The lights in Wusong Town also went out the previous night because a telephone pole was broken by the wind. Also, the power lines in Nanshi, Pudong, and other places were cut by the storm the previous night, plunging several areas into darkness.

Vegetable Prices Soared - The prices of meat and vegetarian dishes in the city's markets, such as fish, shrimp, and other aquatic animals, all increased sharply because they were transported to Shanghai by small boats from other locations. Vegetables like cabbage, taro, edamame, pickled vegetables, and bean sprouts, though transported to the markets from nearby villages in Xujiahui, Jiangwan, and Dachang, were also carried by small boats from more distant villages. Due to the wind and rain the previous night, farmers were unable to harvest their crops. Although a small number of villagers braved the wind and rain to harvest and sell their produce at the markets, the supply was very limited. There was not enough to go around, and the produce quickly sold out. As a result, the vendors in the vegetable markets tripled their profits yesterday, and prices increased by three or four times compared to normal. Even those who offered high prices could not find produce. Salted fish and chicken and duck eggs, which were rarely purchased on normal days, were also impossible to find.

Record of Swedish Prince's Visit 119

Impressions of the Tour of China - Extremely Good

Scheduled to Leave Shanghai for Hong Kong on the 27th to Return Home

To Return in a Year for a Longer Period of Study

Prince Carl of Sweden, accompanied by his friend Mr. Weibel, visited China for sightseeing. After touring Beijing, Shanghai, Tianjin, and other places, he recently returned to Shanghai. Yesterday morning, our reporter interviewed Prince Carl at the Cathay Hotel. The Prince greeted him warmly, and Mr. Weibel also provided hospitality. The Prince, a tall and handsome young man in his twenties, was very polite. He said that he felt honored to visit China and meet with Chairman Lin of the National Government, Executive Yuan President Jiang Jingwei, Vice President Song Ziwen, and other important officials of the National Government. After visiting Beijing, he toured Tianjin, Qingdao, Jinan, and other places. He was very grateful for the warm hospitality of the local officials and people. The impressions he gained during this trip were extremely good and would never be forgotten. He arrived in Beijing on September 4th and went to Tianjin on the 9th for five days. He visited the Forbidden City, the Summer Palace, the library, and Coal Hill. He also climbed the Great Wall and overlooked the entire panorama. He deeply admired the cultural arts of China's long history, but he regretted that he did not have more time to stay. The reporter asked if he would take the opportunity to visit the West Lake in Hangzhou. The Prince smiled and replied that he would like to, but he had already booked a passage on the Changxing Company's Empress of Japan to Hong Kong on the 27th, and then on the Ruodon of the Swedish Post Steamship company, and then return home. If he had time during his short stay in Shanghai, he would definitely visit Hangzhou. After arriving in Hong Kong, he was afraid that he would not be able to visit Guangzhou due to time constraints, which he regretted. He plans to return to China in about a year, at which time he can fully explore and tour the country. He intended to stay in Beiping for at least two months, he stated. The reporter also asked about his impressions of Japan and his personal views on the China-Japan issue. He replied that he had spent about two months in Japan, traveling to famous cities and towns, and the scenery was very pleasant. As for other issues, he had only visited briefly and had not had time for detailed study and research, so he was unable to answer. He was also asked if he planned to visit the Northeast provinces on his next trip to China, where Japan has violently occupied for two years and the 30 million residents are purely Chinese. He said that this had already created a Balkan situation in the Far East, with crises everywhere and ready to erupt. The Prince thought for a moment, paid close attention, and replied that he would like to visit if he had the opportunity. At that time, the Prince was scheduled to visit various factories, so the reporter took his leave.

Mayor Wu Temporarily Assumes Command of the Songhu Garrison

To Take Over Upon Receiving Orders

No Personnel Changes in the Police Department

After Songhu Garrison Commander Dai Ji was ordered to serve as a member of the Fujian Provincial Government and concurrently as the Director of Civil Affairs, he took time to travel north. During this period, the post of garrison commander was temporarily held by Chief of Staff Zhang Xiang. The central government has already determined the official successor, but it has not been announced due to certain reasons. Considering that the Songhu defense is quite important, the position of garrison commander should not be vacant for too long. Yesterday, the Executive Yuan's meeting resolved to appoint Shanghai Mayor Wu Tiecheng to temporarily serve as commander of the Songhu Garrison. Mayor Wu will take over after receiving the order, and Chief of Staff Zhang will handle the handover on the garrison side. The details are as follows:

To Take Over Upon Arrival of the Order in Shanghai 120

Yesterday, the Executive Yuan convened its 126th meeting and passed the appointment of Shanghai Mayor Wu Tiecheng to temporarily serve as Commander of the Songhu Garrison. A reporter from the Central News Agency visited Mayor Wu at the Municipal Government yesterday and asked if he had received the order and when he would take office. According to Mayor Wu, the Executive Yuan's meeting resolved to appoint him as Commander of the Songhu Garrison, but the order had not yet arrived in Shanghai. He had not heard of this beforehand, and President Wang did not mention it when he came to Shanghai a few days ago. He will schedule the takeover after receiving the order. As for the officers of the Garrison Command, he is resolved not to make any changes to their command in order to facilitate familiarity with the work.

Acting Commander Zhang Handles the Handover 121

The Songhu Garrison Command has not yet received an order regarding the Executive Yuan's appointment of Mayor Wu Tiecheng to temporarily serve as commander. According to the acting commander of the Garrison, Zhang Xiang, he has been temporarily holding the post since Commander Dai left Shanghai. Now that the Executive Yuan has appointed Mayor Wu Tiecheng to temporarily serve as commander, he will be responsible for handling all handover procedures when Mayor Wu comes to take office. The command will instruct all departments to prepare for the handover as soon as the order is received.

Important Police Officers Express Intent to Resign 122

Zhang Xiang, Chief of Staff and Acting Commander of the Songhu Garrison Command, met with reporters yesterday and expressed his desire to retire. Zhang said that he had come to Shanghai with Commander Dai not long ago and had just taken office when the January 28th Incident broke out. He then handled the armistice negotiations. After the end of the Shanghai War and the signing of the armistice agreement, he requested to resign but was not approved. Now that Mayor Wu is about to take office, he intends to resign from the post of Chief of Staff in order to take a rest. It is said that the heads of various departments of the Garrison Command have also expressed their intention to resign.

Huang Fu's Delayed Trip to the North 123

Due to the unresolved financial and diplomatic issues in North China

Huang Fu, chairman of the Beiping Political Reorganization Committee, has been residing in Shanghai since visiting Jiang at Lushan, with no intention of returning to Beiping. According to sources in political circles, Huang has met with President Wang and Finance Minister Song several times in Shanghai, but they have not been able to completely resolve the financial and diplomatic issues in North China. Therefore, although Huang has expressed his intention to go north in the coming days, he may not be able to do so for a while. In addition, a member of the Beiping Political Committee arrived in Shanghai yesterday to meet with Huang and report on various situations in North China. Huang did not express any intention to go north. It is said that the member of the Political Committee told others that the plan to reduce military spending in North China has been fully agreed upon. Fang Zhenwu's department has a small number of troops and is no longer a problem. Ji Hongchang's department has been communized and is being dealt with. Although Bao Yulin has decided to resign from the post of director of the Beiping Municipal Police Bureau, Yu Jinhe may not be able to take office for a while.

Shanghai Needs an Airport 124

According to the Continental Daily, Mr. Boli, the manager of the American Continental Airlines, recently went to the United States on business and returned to Shanghai last week. He stated that the future development of Chinese aviation is unlimited and unparalleled in the world today. China has a vast territory, but the development of its transportation system lags behind other countries in the world. The reason for this is that the funding is huge, which leads to simple and crude solutions. The cost of building roads or railways is huge, but opening up an aviation line costs less. It only requires a square area, the construction of an airport, and several ships. Everyone familiar with the world's aviation situation feels that the lack of a suitable airport in Shanghai is a shortcoming in transportation for the prosperity of Shanghai. It is an urgent matter for the interests of Shanghai and all of China. For example, the city of Havana in Cuba recently spent about 300,000 yuan to build an airport to benefit 500,000 residents. Shanghai has 3 million residents and cannot even keep up, which is lamentable. Mr. Boli also said that 32 Curtiss Hawk aircraft purchased by the National Government from the Curtiss-Wright Company have been delivered, including three that were shipped on the Lincoln President last week. The remaining 11 will be shipped within 30 days. It is noted that Mr. Boli is also the vice president of the Curtiss-Wright Company.
