Japanese Yarn Impersonates Domestic Goods 130

Ten Factories Secretly Import Large Quantities of Japanese Yarn

Forge Domestic Tax Receipts for Inspection

The Court Held its First Trial Yesterday

The Case was Adjourned for Ten Days

Ten factories including the Gongzu Socks Factory, Sanyang Cotton Weaving Factory, Jiuyi Weaving Factory, Dingxin Cloth Factory, Yudong Socks Factory, Junchang Dyeing and Weaving Factory, Yunzhou Dyeing and Weaving Factory, Yongyuan Mercerizing Factory, Yixing Company, and Tonghe Dyeing and Weaving Factory, have secretly imported large quantities of Japanese yarn, added artificial modifications, falsely claimed that they were produced by Shenxin No. 5 Yarn Factory, and sold them in the market, deceiving the Chinese people and affecting the reputation of Shenxin. Recently, Rong Weiren, the manager of Shenxin No. 5 Factory, filed a criminal self-accusation against the managers of the ten fake factories, Yu Xifan, Chen Zhongxian, Wang Liwei, Sun Xinzu, Yu Yuxin, Zhou Songmao, Chai Zhixiang, Zhao Bingnan, Wang Gensheng, and Guan Bingqing, requesting that they be punished according to law and demanding compensation for damages of 200,000 yuan. According to the plaintiff, recently, domestic compatriots, in view of the increasingly urgent foreign insults, have successively boycotted Japanese goods. Those who sell and purchase them are ridiculed as traitors and their personalities are demeaned. The raw materials used by the defendants' factories have always been purchased from Japanese yarn factories. They are deeply afraid that once they are exposed, their commercial morality will be lost and they will be abandoned by the Chinese people. Therefore, they disregarded the violation of criminal law. When they reported to the Suzhou-Zhejiang-Anhui District Unified Tax Bureau of the Ministry of Finance for transportation before their products were made, according to the procedures, they had to submit the tax certificate of the imported raw materials at the same time. They actually transformed the tax certificate of the Limaping brand of the Japanese Dakang Yarn Factory into the Renzhong brand of Shenxin No. 5 Factory to deceive the public. The bureau discovered the above incident and notified the factory to send personnel to investigate and verify the truth. The plaintiff's factory believes that the defendants' behavior not only violates criminal law, but also hinders commerce. Therefore, a lawsuit is filed in accordance with the law. It is clear that the defendants' actions of falsifying official documents are sufficient to cause damage to others, to hold them out for use, or to intend to deceive others as forging trademarks and trade names. Article 225 and other articles 233 and 268 of the Criminal Law all have clear provisions for punishment. Now the defendants have falsified the tax certificate of the Unified Tax Administration of the Ministry of Finance and the trade names and trademarks of this factory for use, which is sufficient to cause damage to this factory and to deceive others. Their intention to violate the above cases is obvious. Furthermore, the fine yarn required by the defendants' factories has always been Japanese goods. Since the September 18th Incident, in view of the enthusiasm of the compatriots to boycott Japanese goods, they have often falsified the tax certificates when reporting for transportation. This is not the first time. They forget righteousness when they see profit and have no conscience. Because they did not obtain conclusive evidence, this factory endured the damage and did not act. This time, the old trick was used again, which was discovered. After the occurrence of this case, people in the community are confused, which has greatly damaged the reputation of this factory, and the damage suffered is extremely serious. Therefore, this lawsuit is filed with your court in accordance with the law, and the defendants are separately detained and tried in accordance with Article 74 of the Criminal Law and Article 225 of the same law, and attached a private lawsuit, requesting that the defendants be jointly and severally liable for compensation for the damages incurred. 200,000 yuan, etc. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Liu Yugui of the Criminal Court of the First Special District Local Court held a trial. Most of the defendants did not come in person, only their lawyers appeared in court and requested a postponement. After the plaintiff's lawyer, Sun Zuji, stated the intention of the prosecution, the court ordered an adjournment for ten days for trial.

Chen Jiageng Generously Donates Over 70,000 Yuan for Yellow River Flood Relief 131

This year's Yellow River flood, although not as extensive as the Jianghuai flood of the 20th year of the Republic (1931), is extremely severe. The flooded area covers approximately six million square meters, and about two million people are displaced. The National Government, for the sake of relief, established the Yellow River Flood Relief Committee under the Executive Yuan, specifically to handle disaster relief, work relief, and sanitation matters. The committee was established immediately after Finance Minister Song returned to the country. However, substantial funds are required for disaster relief and work relief, but the government's allocation is limited. Furthermore, due to commercial depression, it was decided not to solicit donations from the public. Just when funds were urgently needed, the committee received 73,539.58 yuan remitted by Mr. Chen Jiageng from Singapore on behalf of the overseas Chinese community there. The committee immediately sent a telegram to express its gratitude and praise his righteous spirit. It is hoped that domestic and foreign philanthropists can all be as generous as the overseas Chinese in Singapore, so that the disaster victims can be benefited, and the virtue will be boundless.

China Merchants Electric Tramway Route 2 Circular Route Trial Run Yesterday 132

In order to facilitate passengers and eliminate the need for Route 4 to turn around at Laoximen, the China Merchants Electric Tramway Company has added a branch line from Heping Road to Nanyang Bridge, as well as additional routes in areas such as the Shanghai Garrison. Now that various projects have been completed one after another, the company's Traffic Section Chief Lu Zhonglin, Du Ningru, together with Engineering Section Chief Song Zhihou, and Public Works Bureau's Fourth Section Chief Zhang Dengyi participated in and supervised the first trial run yesterday afternoon at 2:00 PM. They led personnel from the traffic and engineering departments, starting from Nanyang Bridge, passing Laoximen, Shangwenmen, turning into Daxing Street, passing the Local Government Office, through the Shanghai Garrison, along the Bund, passing Xuejiabang, Dongjiadu, Guan Bridge, Xiaodongmen, along Zhonghua Road, passing Dadongmen, Xiaonanmen, Shangwenmen, Laoximen, and finally reaching Nanyang Bridge. This is the Route 2 circular route. The trial run was very satisfactory. At 4:30 PM, the tram returned to the company. Announcement 133

For the purpose of announcement, the Route 2 circular route is scheduled to officially open on the 20th of this month. Driving Matters 134

(1) Route 2 trams leaving the factory will have red route signs with four stations marked with red lines, and black route signs with ten stations marked with blue lines. When arriving at the Shanghai Garrison, circular route tickets will be sold. Zang Qifang of the Northeast Association Speaks Painfully About the National Crisis 136

The day before yesterday was the anniversary of the September 18th Incident and the loss of the Northeast. Meetings were held everywhere during the day to commemorate the event, and entertainment venues were closed to express mourning. At 7:30 PM, the YMCA invited Mr. Zang Qifang of the Northeast Association to give a speech at the Eight Immortals Bridge Hall. His words were extremely painful, and everyone who attended the speech was deeply moved. Mr. Zang's topic was "The Understanding of the National Crisis That Chinese People Should Have." Here is a record of his speech:

The Seriousness of the National Crisis 137

Ladies and gentlemen, on this second anniversary night of the September 18th Incident, we gather in a room to commemorate the national crisis. Despite such strong winds and heavy rain, you are still willing to come, which shows your deep pain and hatred and your unforgetting of the lost territory. What I want to talk about today is the understanding of the national crisis that Chinese people should have. The Northeast has been lost for two years. To what extent is it serious in these two years? This is really not an easy question to answer. Now let us first examine it from the facts. What was the situation in the Northeast before two years ago? At that time, the Northeast was still in the hands of our Chinese people. What kind of manifestations did the Japanese have with their premeditation? To be specific, from the Sino-Japanese War of 1894-95 to today, a full forty years, excluding the recent two years of the Northeast's loss, the Japanese have been preparing every day for the previous thirty-eight years. Since the beginning of the Republic of China, the Japanese have secretly transported large amounts of money from their country to the Northeast every year, bribing people in the Northeast government. It sounds bizarre and unbelievable. At that time, all institutions and even factories, from the chief executives to the small employees, were rarely not bribed by the Japanese. There were several mining companies and coal and iron companies, all of which were jointly run by China and Japan on the surface, with both Chinese and Japanese responsible persons, but in fact, the Chinese only took the money and did nothing. The Japanese even said that the Chinese were working hard and gave them additional remuneration besides their original salaries. So everyone lost their conscience for money and didn't care about anything, and secret news was supplied continuously. If someone asked those employees, "Why do you lose your conscience and take Japanese money?" They would all answer like this, "If I don't take it, someone else will take it. Everyone takes it. Who can blame whom?" In addition, the Japanese also sent various experts in agriculture, commerce, mining, and education, etc., to various institutions in the Northeast as consultants. They were not ordinary consultants, but were working under the orders of the Japanese government. When they returned home, each person had a detailed report. It is really painful to say. At that time, the Northeast had already secretly fallen. The Japanese were determined to destroy the Northeast, always using the excuse of surplus goods and too many people. In fact, Japan itself has enough to supply. Therefore, the reason why they want to seize my Northeast is that they must have it to compete with the major powers of Britain and the United States in the world. Moreover, they will not be satisfied with just getting the Northeast. Soon they will take another step to peep into North China and swallow my entire country. The Yuan's treatment of the Song, the Qing's treatment of the Ming, and the Japanese's treatment of the Republic of China are all the same steps. The Japanese are very familiar with Chinese history. If this continues, the Chinese will inevitably be bound to wait for death. Please also take a look at the current Japanese facilities in the Northeast. In general, the essentials of establishing a country are: first, finance; second, transportation; third, security. In the past, the currency in the Northeast was extremely inconsistent. Liaoning banknotes could not be used in Jilin, and Jilin banknotes could not be used in Jiang Province. Now, the paper money of the (Manchukuo) Central Bank is circulating everywhere. As long as an old coin from the former official silver house is stamped with a (Manchukuo) Central Bank stamp, it can circulate without hindrance. In this way, there is no problem with the unification of finance in the Northeast. As for transportation and security, since the Japanese took over, they have been fulfilling their wishes in every way. The plan of the (Manchukuo) railway network is exhausted, and the investigation of household registration and the confiscation of firearms have made it impossible for the volunteer army to gain a foothold. In another year, they will be deeply rooted, and the future will be even more unimaginable. At present, domestic natural and man-made disasters, in the future, the people of Shandong, Hebei, and Shanxi provinces will be willing to go to the Northeast to reclaim land for him because of their insecure lives. It is absolutely possible for the Japanese to further occupy my entire country. Please, those who care about national interests, like you, think carefully about this serious situation.

The Japanese's Heinous Methods 138

There are about two methods that the Japanese use to deal with our Chinese people: (1) The policy of using Chinese to control Chinese. The most obvious is to support my revolution at the end of the Qing Dynasty. He absolutely does not want my revolution to succeed. He wants to take advantage of my revolution to loot. Since the Republic of China, several civil wars have been instigated by the Japanese behind the scenes. Zhang Zuolin wanted to enter the Pass and ask about the Central Plains. He was afraid that the Japanese would cause trouble behind him. The Japanese said, "Just go ahead and cause trouble. You can rest assured about the rear. We will definitely help." So there was the Fengzhi War. The Anfu clique's assistance from the Japanese is even more obvious. The mutiny of Guo Songling in Fengtian (actually, it cannot be said to be a defection). If the Japanese had not helped Zhang, Guo would definitely not have failed. At that time, it was Honjo Shigeru, who launched the September 18th Incident, who dug trenches for Zhang. In short, the Japanese are always trying to divide China. After the September 18th Incident, they used puppets to organize a government and bribed old warlords to disturb North China. It goes without saying. He always uses the policy of using Chinese to control Chinese. He feels that it is not necessary to use great force to fight these endless yellow people. He wants to save strength and participate in the World War. Therefore, he is now verbally saying that he is friendly and wants to use my government. Unfortunately, the authorities are confused and will often be greatly deceived. (2) The policy of psychological conquest. The Japanese know the ancient saying that attacking the mind is the most important thing. Therefore, they always want to conquer the Chinese psychologically, wanting my Chinese people to regard the Japanese as gods and surrender unconditionally. I have personally seen many people who study in the army in Japan, and their minds have been conquered by the Japanese. He wants you to believe that only he has a solution, and you have no solution. He hates the Chinese people who will always resist Japan and swear to die to resist Japan the most. Therefore, if it is someone like Ma Zhanshan, he will falsely accuse him to death. He hopes that all those who resist Japan will die, so that they can feel at ease and happy. On our side, only those who will always resist Japan and swear to die to resist Japan are worthy of being called true patriots and descendants of the Yellow Emperor of true gods. Whether we are radicals, advocating desperate fighting, or those who endure humiliation and burden, the first thing to decide is the issue of people. First, you have to ask you, does this person have self-confidence? If so, then you must firmly believe that the Chinese nation will have the hope of revival. Second, you have to ask you whether this person can have a spirit of sacrifice. If so, then you should not be threatened in any way, such as Mount Tai collapsing in front of you, and your color does not change. You should not give up the responsibility of resisting Japan for any right, and swear to eradicate Japanese imperialism and its running dogs, so as to revitalize my Chinese nation as an independent country in the world.

Shanghai Municipal Bureau of Public Works Rushes to Repair East and West Embankments 140

The Breach in the East Embankment Has Been Blocked

The West Embankment Is Also Being Repaired

On the second of this month, a hurricane suddenly struck, and the raging waves surged like mountains. The East and West Embankments were both breached. The East Embankment, including the Aiyuli Shishou Chenfu Rongqiang Xia Luyibin and other companies, had more than ten breaches. The remaining earth embankments, which were only one or two-tenths of the original, were about four kilometers long. Although this hurricane was not as severe as the one in the 20th year of the Republic (1931), the wind direction in the 20th year attacked the embankment head-on. Except for the top being damaged, the rest was still intact. The wind on the second of this month swept along the embankment, and the entire embankment was attacked, so the degree of damage and danger was far greater than in the 20th year. After the accident, Shen, the Director of the Municipal Bureau of Public Works, accompanied by his staff, went to investigate and reported to the Municipal Government for allocation of funds for emergency repairs, and decided to block the breaches first. Now this task has been completed by the Bureau's workers, and the remaining damaged earth embankments will be repaired by recruiting workers separately, which can also be started within one or two days. As for the embankment along Jungong Road in Xitang, from the water and electricity plant to the naval hospital, the soil on the side of the embankment was washed away by the hurricane and tidal waves, and the roots of the planted trees were all exposed. The Ding Wu Bureau has sent workers to rush to repair it, first repairing the soil near the roots to avoid the withering of thousands of trees. This project was completed yesterday. In addition, the stone embankment in Wusong and the section west of the fort to the border of Shishan County also had several breaches, and Wu Mufeng was the most dangerous. The Bureau of Public Works sent personnel on the 18th, accompanied by a large number of workers, and materials such as sacks, to rush to repair it in the rain. The Bureau also sent personnel to investigate the damaged stone embankments in Wusong Outer Ma Road and Fort Taiwan, and formulated a repair plan, together with the main project plan for repairing the East Embankment, and submitted it to the Municipal Government for appropriation of funds. It is said that the entire emergency repair project requires filling more than 40,000 cubic meters of soil, and it will take at least 50 days to complete. According to the report of the Observatory the day before yesterday, the hurricane will attack Shanghai for the second time. After hearing the news, the Bureau sent a large number of workers on the 19th, carrying emergency repair materials such as sacks, to the most dangerous location in the East Embankment to carry out the most important emergency work to prevent any eventuality.

Baoshan County Party Headquarters Sends Telegram Opposing the Provincial Government's Surcharge and Reward 141

The Baoshan County Party Headquarters believes that the Jiangsu Provincial Government's method of clearing old taxes in various counties is inappropriate, and sent a telegram to the Party Headquarters of various counties, requesting them to jointly submit a request to the Provincial Party Headquarters to oppose it unanimously. The text of the telegram is as follows: To the Party Headquarters of various counties in Jiangsu Province, and forwarded to various organizations: The Jiangsu Provincial Government has decided to clear the old taxes in various counties due to the large amount of arrears. This move is originally an urgent plan, but it should not encroach on the original tax revenue, so that it can be helpful to the facts. This time, the Finance Department sent personnel to various counties to clear the land tax for the years 16 to 20 of the Republic of China, and to use 10% of the actual amount collected to recover the old arrears over the years as a bonus. The provincial regulations did not explicitly stipulate that the local surtax should be included in the reward. However, according to legal principles, the land tax committee declared that whether it is the regular tax or the surtax, all should be rewarded. If so, the disadvantages have already arisen before the benefits are seen. Furthermore, (1) the regular tax and surtax of several counties have always been divided. For example, the late payment fines, etc., are only added to the regular tax. Therefore, the reward of 10% can only be charged under the provincial tax items. (2) The old arrears of our county for each year have already been included in the budget for each year for the purpose of repaying the loans of various institutions. After the reward, it will be impossible to make up for it. (3) The arrears of grain tax are the result of ineffective collection. Giving rewards for completion is tantamount to encouraging the trend of ineffective collection. In the future, those who collect effectively will also hope for bonuses, and will be even more ineffective. How can they improve the future? (4) According to the customs of our county, the collection of this year's grain tax will end at the end of the year, and at most 30% to 40% will be collected. The rest will be in arrears until the next year and then collected one after another. The accumulated arrears over the years are very large. After the January 28th Incident, our county bore the brunt of the disaster and suffered the most. The funds of various institutions are in huge deficit and difficult to maintain. If another 10% is extracted from the old surtax arrears as a reward, it will be even more difficult to maintain the progress of the cause. In order to take into account the future of local undertakings, our association dares to send a telegram to your association, please jointly submit a request to the Provincial Party Headquarters, which will be forwarded to the Provincial Government, ordering the Finance Department to immediately cancel the reward for local surtax, and ordering the county government to stop the reward. We are impatiently awaiting your orders. Signed, Baoshan County Party Affairs Reorganization Committee

Trial of the Case of Beating Niece to Death 143

Blood Stains on Clothes Proven to Be Human Blood

Wang Zhangshi Claims Child Died from Fall

The Case Was Adjourned for Retrial

Wang Zhangshi, a Ningbo woman, 46 years old, residing on the third floor of the Tianlu Candy Tea and Food Store at 209 Caishi Road in the French Concession, is a widow with one son and one daughter. She is known for her violent temper and often abuses her daughter Xiuying (a widowed worker at the Fuchang Tobacco Company)'s three-year-old adopted daughter, Wang Fugen (i.e., her niece), to the point that she suffers from illness and moans in bed. Not only does she not give her medical treatment, but on the evening of the 3rd of this month, at about 7:00 PM, because the child cried and angered her, she beat the child's chin with a piece of firewood, and the child died instantly. Wang wrapped the child's body, took it out, and threw it into a creek near Xieqiao to destroy the evidence. The incident was discovered by the second landlord, Yang Zhushi, and neighbor Zhang Jinan, who reported it to the police. Wang was arrested, and a search was conducted for the child's body, but it was not found. Only a small white cotton short shirt (an undershirt) worn by Wang with blood stains and a piece of white cloth from the bed were found and sent to the Second Special District Local Court for trial. The court sent the blood-stained shirt to the Zhenru Forensic Research Institute for examination. After detailed examination by the medical officer of the institute, the seven blood stains on the shirt were divided into seven numbers. Numbers one to six were confirmed to be human blood without any doubt, and the blood stain of number seven had been washed with soap and still had soap marks. Three copies of the autopsy report were prepared and sent back to the court. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Wang Gangxi conducted a trial in the First Criminal Court. The defendant Wang Zhangshi was brought to the court first. Judge: What did you use to beat the child to death? Defendant: She actually fell from the bed and died. I was collecting clothes on the drying platform. Judge: How high is the bed from the ground? Defendant: About the same height as the table (referring to the news reporter's seat in the courtroom, about one foot two feet high). Judge: How could she die from falling from that height? Defendant: The child has been sick for two months. Judge: Has she been treated? Defendant: I took her to the Siming Hospital twice. Judge: Do you have the prescription? Defendant: The prescription was thrown away by my daughter. Judge: What disease did she have? Defendant: Like milk tuberculosis. Judge: What did she look like when she fell? Defendant: I came down from the drying platform and saw that she was not responding. Judge: Was she injured? Defendant: I was so frightened that I didn't see clearly. Judge: Was her head broken and bleeding? Defendant: She fell to the ground, and there was a wound on her forehead and bleeding. Judge: What time did she fall? Defendant: It was a little after seven o'clock. Judge: What time did you take the body out? Defendant: After she didn't respond, after a while, I took it out. Judge: Why did you take it out? Defendant: I was so scared that I took it out and asked Xiao San to throw it away. He wanted three yuan, and I gave him three yuan. Judge: Was it wrapped in cloth when you took it out? Defendant: It was wrapped in old cloth and dressed in clothes. Judge: Since you took it out, why did you lie to the neighbors that the child was at her grandmother's house? Defendant: Her words were vague. Judge: What exactly did you use to beat her to death? Tell the truth, and you can still be forgiven. Defendant: She is my niece, I would never beat her to death. Judge: Where did the blood stains on your clothes come from? Defendant: I don't know. And she stammered. The judge said that the clothes have now been proven by the forensic doctor to be human blood. Where did it come from? The defendant bowed her head and said nothing. The judge asked if it was because the child was crying and she beat her. Beating the child is a common occurrence. Did you accidentally beat her to death? You might as well tell the truth honestly. Defendant: I have never beaten her. At this point, the judge summoned the witness, the second landlord Yang Zhushi (69 years old), to the court and ordered her to swear to tell the truth. After Zhushi swore, she testified that Wang lived in my house with her mother and daughter and the child, a total of three people. Zhang often beat the child and I heard her crying. On the evening of that day, she beat her again and I heard her crying. Then I saw her carrying her out. I didn't think much of it, but the neighbors said that the child was beaten to death. After a while, I saw her returning to the room empty-handed and closed the door. I and Mr. Zhang (i.e., Zhang Jinan) went to knock on the door and asked her where the child had gone. She said she was at someone else's house. I said I wanted to see her. The people around said that you had already beaten her to death. Tell me the truth, and I won't send you away. She then said that she had beaten her to death with one slap and thrown her away. I then reported it to the police. Then the witness Zhang Jinan was summoned to the court. His testimony was the same as Yang Zhushi's. The judge also asked Wang Wangshi if you were on good terms with the second landlord. Wang replied that I don't go to her house, but it's just like that. Judge: Did you hear what the two witnesses said? Defendant: I heard them say that I beat her to death, so I beat her to death. I have no way. At this point, the judge appointed lawyer Huang Jue as counsel for the defendant in court. Later, lawyer Huang requested an adjournment for defense, citing the importance of the case and the need for time to review the files. The court approved it, and then ordered that the defendant be retried on the 23rd and remanded for instructions.

Husband Seeks Divorce After Wife Disappears for Six Years 144

Cheng Yongsheng, a native of Shexian County, Anhui, is 32 years old and works at the telegraph office. He lives near Yuhang Bridge South Yan Gongtang in the city. In the first month of the 14th year of the Republic of China (1925), he married Zhou Ruxia, a woman from the same township, through matchmaking. She disappeared soon after and has been gone for six years. Cheng Yongsheng has hired a lawyer to file for divorce in the local court, citing that her whereabouts are unknown, and has requested public notice. The gist of his petition is that the defendant's life or death is unknown and has been for more than three years. The opposing party is wandering and extravagant and not at ease at home. On the ninth day of the fifth month of the 16th year of the Republic of China (1927), she took the opportunity to run away without a trace. The plaintiff initially hoped that she would change her mind, but the defendant took the lead and repeatedly sent letters through lawyer Lin on the 28th day of the ninth month of the 16th year of the Republic of China (1927), requesting divorce and alimony. Then, in addition to requesting a divorce, she requested the return of her dowry. Finally, in addition to requesting a divorce, she requested to take back her daughter, Zhenbao, who was three years old at the time (now nine years old). He requested that public notice be granted. Yesterday, Judge He summoned the plaintiff, who did not appear. Only the representing lawyer appeared in court to state the previous circumstances and claimed that the defendant Zhou Ruxia's mother and brother have both died. The defendant's life or death has been unknown for more than three years. The judge said that although the letters from lawyer Lin proved that the defendant was willing to divorce, the point of whether her life or death is unknown still needs to be investigated. The representing lawyer was ordered to investigate whether the defendant has any family members or relatives and await verification.

Page 12

Ministry of Interior Approves No Extension for Physician Certification Deadline 147

Reply from the Ministry of Interior to the National Physicians' Association Regarding the Extension of the Deadline for Alternate Physician Certification

The National Physicians' Association previously received letters from the Hankou Huaining and other Physicians' Associations stating that since the Ministry of Interior's alternate physician certification measures were promulgated, a year had passed. However, due to the vastness of China and the prevalence of natural disasters and man-made calamities, those residing in remote rural towns or living as travelers may not have seen the official notice, and some may have been missed. They requested the General Association to petition the authorities to extend the deadline in order to achieve universal coverage. The National Physicians' Association petitioned the authorities to postpone the deadline. Yesterday, they received Reply No. 39 from the Ministry of Interior, which stated: "The petition is noted. The temporary measures for alternate physician certification were promulgated in August of the 21st year of the Republic of China, with a one-year deadline, starting from the date of receipt in each locality, with the provision that (areas affected by bandits and special circumstances are excluded). The dates of receipt in each locality varied, generally falling between September and October. The situation described in the petition is therefore not inappropriate. The request for an extension should not be considered." It is reported that the association has already issued a notice to the Huaining, Hankou, and other physicians' associations to take note of the Ministry of Interior's reply.

Chinese and Foreign Relief Society Sends Personnel to Investigate Nanhui Typhoon Disaster 149

The Chinese and Foreign Relief Society received a telegram from Nanhui County stating that the area was devastated by a hurricane and heavy rain on September 12th and 13th, causing the collapse of embankments and flooding. The society immediately dispatched specialists to conduct on-site investigations. According to their report, the affected area includes districts 1, 2, and 4, with District 1 being the most severely affected. The tidal surge was extremely strong, causing damage to crops and houses. The flooded area covers more than 200 square miles, including over 100,000 mu of farmland. If the floodwaters do not recede, the autumn harvest is hopeless. Approximately 20,000 mu have been affected. More than 10,000 people are living outdoors, exposed to the wind and rain, and have lost their homes. Not only do the embankments need immediate repair, but the Wanggongtang Harbor has also become heavily silted over the years and urgently needs dredging, otherwise, the consequences will be unthinkable. The society considers the immediate needs of emergency work and disaster relief to be the most important and urgent tasks. However, fundraising is difficult and they are seeking donations. If Heaven helps those who help themselves, they will be able to proceed actively.

Recent Charitable Deeds of the Pushan Villa 150

The Pushan Villa specializes in burying unclaimed and exposed corpses in the Chinese and foreign concessions, which is related to local public health. From January to August of this year, it collected a total of 17,567 coffins of all sizes, provided 7,998 coffins of all sizes, and provided 36,335 free medical consultations. It is reported that since the year of Wuchen, the villa has been burying corpses found floating in rivers and temporarily interring corpses in the interior of Jiangsu and Zhejiang, and has collected 72,123 corpses to date. Furthermore, in the summer of last year, after seeing reports in Suzhou about an epidemic, General Director Wang Yiting appointed Director Wang Junsheng to investigate in Suzhou. It was determined that the city's river was polluted and a health hazard, so efforts were made to clean it up. A total of 383 coffins exposed around the city and suburbs were buried, 2,257 dead animals such as floating rats, cats, and dogs were collected from the river, 119 boats of garbage were dredged, 35 dried-up public wells were repaired, and 20 storage boxes for dead animals were installed. The river water was cleaned, which was a great convenience for the residents and beneficial for drinking water. However, due to the decline of various industries, donations to the villa have become scarce, and expenses have become increasingly large, and funding has become increasingly depleted. One person's efforts are not enough. It is necessary to rely on the collective efforts of the community to succeed. It is hoped that people from all walks of life will consider public health and contribute generously to maintain this good cause.

Publication of Historical Materials on Diplomacy During the Late Qing Dynasty 153

Rich in Content and Extremely Valuable

"Historical Materials on Diplomacy During the Late Qing Dynasty" was compiled by Wang Yifu of Huangyan, Beiping. It contains nearly all of the unequal treaties of the Guangxu reign of the Qing Dynasty, the establishment procedures for consular jurisdiction and the loss of tariff autonomy, telegraphs about war negotiations, trade boundary divisions, as well as transcripts of meetings between the Zongli Yamen and the ministers. Such confidential manuscripts were not disclosed in the former Qing Dynasty. Wang served in the Imperial Secretariat for nearly 20 years, personally copying them and storing them at home. His son, Xi Yin, proofread and edited them into a book, and searched for important documents from the Xuantong reign of the Qing Dynasty to continue the compilation. He also wrote subject indexes, connecting things according to type, to facilitate checking. The entire book totals 120 volumes and is truly a valuable resource for those studying modern Chinese diplomacy. Now, British and French people, seeing the book's thorough and comprehensive content, have discussed translating the index to facilitate study. Since its publication, there has been a constant stream of domestic and foreign orders, and requests for special arrangements to facilitate distribution. However, there are few copies remaining. Once sold out, it will not be easy to reprint. Those who study the history of the Qing Dynasty should order as soon as possible. The general distributor is Nai Zi Fu Guan Dong Dian 7, Beiping. Local distributors in this port include Cheng Xuemen, Mao Zhenchu of the Chen Bao Guan, the Da Gong Bao branch on Jiujiang Road, and the Hua Tong Book Store at Wangping Street. Samples can be requested by mail.

Xinghualou's 70th Anniversary Celebration The Xinghualou on No. 4 Malu has been open for 70 years. Spring and Autumn

Setting the Stage 164

— Bing Ding

The Chinese are most adept at the art of (setting the stage), even foreign architects admire them to the point of prostration. Just look at the tall Western-style buildings in Shanghai, aren't they first (scaffolded)? For example, the twenty-two story Four Banks Joint Savings Society warehouse currently under construction on Jing'an Temple Road, is covered with very high bamboo scaffolding, densely layered. Isn't its artistry remarkable? Also, families celebrating or mourning, and new businesses opening, must erect many scaffolds to create a spectacle. To the laborers who build these scaffolds, it's truly an easy job. With just a few bamboo poles and some bamboo strips, in less than half a day, they can erect a dignified and imposing decorated shed.

The art of building scaffolds is astonishing. A few rough and strong laborers in blue cloth, haphazardly erect a few bamboo poles, tie them together with strips of bamboo, and layer upon layer, in a moment, the scaffolding is completed, laying the groundwork for a magnificent and splendid structure. Or, they adorn it with colorful decorations and dazzling lights, making it appear vibrant and flourishing; in reality, it's just a bamboo scaffold.

It's the same with a person. If you want to create a spectacle and raise your status, you must start with (setting the stage). Friends who don't (set the stage) are bound to be left behind in today's society. They will be ridiculed, scorned, and mocked. This is the result of (not setting the stage). Scaffolding is extremely important for building houses; scaffolding is also crucial for (the art of getting along in the world).

Officials need to put on an official air, managers and directors need to put on the airs of managers and directors. Therefore, capitalists need to put on the airs of capitalists. Even servants in mansions, teachers in schools, compradores in foreign firms, and procuresses and prostitutes in brothels, all have their own airs to display their status. However, the wonder of (setting the stage) is subtle and difficult to put into words. Where it can be set, it must be set; where it cannot be set, it's best to dismantle it quickly. Only then can it be considered the art of (setting the stage). For example, bureaucrats (put on airs) when they see ordinary people; but when they meet their superiors, or their wives or concubines, they must dismantle their fragile façade. Managers and directors (put on airs) when they see their staff, but when they see old shareholders, they must dismantle their feeble facade. Being able to set up and dismantle is the mark of an expert in (setting the stage).

Friends who are on good terms achieve good fortune through the (art of flattery) and become successful, of course they need to put on airs to show off their power. I believe that putting on airs everywhere with a puffed-up chest is not necessarily a loss of a heroic nature. Only those experts in (offensive airs) who set up and dismantle them haphazardly are chilling, does a hero have this ability to (bend and stretch)? But, setting the stage is ultimately a matter of pride for a hero!

Rickshaw Pullers 165

— Xian Xian

A certain celebrity advocates not riding rickshaws because having (people) pull (people) is (inhumane), so if one must ride, it should be a car, or better yet, just use one's own two legs and (walk instead of riding). That's right, by (practicing what one preaches) like this, there's no fear that the rickshaw pullers will all starve to death, and thus China's (barbarism) can be reduced a little. But we uninspired and awkward friends, cannot afford to ride in cars, and our legs are not strong enough to rely on walking alone, so we have no choice but to rely on rickshaws. Although (people pulling people) is somewhat (inhumane), rickshaw pullers still depend on us (inhumane philanthropists) to avoid ending up in a ditch.

Although people often argue with rickshaw pullers over a single penny and even insult their parents and ancestors for eighteen generations, when they pick up a pen to describe the lives of rickshaw pullers, they express one hundred and twenty percent sympathy and pity. Even the beads of sweat on the rickshaw pullers' backs become the author's tears, although in reality, when the rickshaw puller is out of breath, the author is scolding, ("Pig, why don't you run faster!")

The only (virtue) of rickshaw pullers is naturally (honesty in returning lost items), but even robbers sometimes have moments of kindness, let alone rickshaw pullers. But, in fact, rickshaw pullers who are (dishonest in returning lost items) are more common than those who are (honest in returning lost items). As for those who don't roll their eyes and insist on adding two or three cents to the fare just because the destination is in an alley, and who don't get scolded by the passengers, they are as rare as stars in the morning sky.

On North Sichuan Road, Avenue Joffre, the Bund, and in the residential areas of foreign dignitaries and high-class Chinese, rickshaw pullers are indeed more pitiful than dogs. Especially when a customer sits sideways in the corner of the rickshaw, their feet almost touching the rickshaw puller's back, fully demonstrating the (art of riding in a rickshaw), the rickshaw puller has no choice but to show off their ability to compete with cars. But the rickshaw pullers who pick up customers at the train station or pier have a different face, and they are always walking (slowly) and stopping halfway. They will then dump the rickshaw and shout, ("I won't pull this long distance without more money!")

Using Toes as Watch Charm 166

— Nu Xia

There is a retired military officer named Dengtu in Heidelberg. He had won many battles during the European war, until his left foot was injured and he had to leave the military. At that time, because his ankle was shattered, it could not be cured, so the doctor sawed off his foot. He was very reluctant to part with his round foot, and repeatedly asked the doctor to cut off his second and third toes and return them to him. Then, he soaked them in medicine, and then dried them in the sun. When they were hard and smooth, like snails, he sent them to a jewelry store to be made into a watch charm, which he wore on his chest every day. He still strokes and kisses them from time to time, considering them ten times more precious than medals won with blood and flesh.

Fourth Company Commander of the Northeast 167

— Zhang Henshui

Chapter Fifteen: The Departing Guest Leaves Behind a Bashful Smile of Tenderness, The Visiting Person Brings Old Malice and Opens a Troubled Heart

He said, "I heard that Master Gan Er is already doing something in the city, and he is no longer working with his brother." Gui Zhi blushed and said, "Mother Liu, please don't mention this person. I hate this person to the core. You don't know, one day I delivered goods to their house, and they coaxed me out. I am a girl, and a poor one at that, what can I do to deal with people? I can only endure it. So even now, whenever I hear Gan Jizhi's name, my head hurts." Mother Liu heard that this was why she was dissatisfied with the Gan family, and it was no wonder that the more she talked about the Gan family, the more she blushed. Seeing this, she realized that it would be better for her to say less. So she didn't dare to stay long, and after talking for a few words, she left. But Mother Liu's character was different from Gui Zhi's. She thought that associating with rich people was a matter of face, and anyway, she would only take advantage of them, not the other way around. Moreover, she was an aging old woman, and the Gan family didn't mind her visiting. So after she heard these words at Gui Zhi's house, in less than twenty-four hours, those words were completely conveyed to Mrs. Gan's ears. Mrs. Gan was not only not angry when she heard this, but she was actually delighted for a while. She felt that she had been prescient in opposing Jizhi's association with Gui Zhi, knowing that Gui Zhi would not be able to cooperate with him. This news had to be made known to Jizhi, so that he could regret it a little. However, at this time, Jizhi was teaching at a school in Nan Yuan Da Hong Men, which was also in the suburbs. To transmit the news from the western suburbs to the southern suburbs would take considerable effort, so it wasn't until two months later that Jizhi returned to the city from Nan Yuan to buy things and encountered a relative, that he got some news from the relative's mouth. However, it was not easy for him to leave his school. Counting the principal, teachers, staff, and workers, there were only four people in total. A round trip from Nan Yuan to Haidian would take a whole day, how could he leave the school for a day? Another month later, he got a holiday, and he took advantage of an early morning to rush to Haidian in the western suburbs. (192)

Earth Store Bodhisattva's Birthday 168

— Chen Zhou

The sun had just jumped into the mountain gully, and Lingling was pestering her grandma to stick incense for Earth Store Bodhisattva. Grandma, unable to resist her pestering, said, ("It's too early! Earth Store Bodhisattva won't open his eyes until it's completely dark!")

Lingling had nothing to say! She ran to the yard and stood there, standing like a statue, anxiously watching the sky. The sky finally darkened, so dark that the banana tree standing on the other side of the yard could not be seen clearly. She ran back again, calling out to her grandma, saying, ("Now we can stick incense!")

("Why are you in such a hurry? You can do it after you eat!") ("Hmm, I don't want to! Didn't you just say to stick incense when it's completely dark?")

But in the end, she sat down to eat with her grandma and brother. She only ate half a bowl of rice, and then put down her chopsticks and said to her grandma, ("Grandma, can we...")

("Wait until I finish eating!")

Today, Grandma seemed to be deliberately teasing Lingling, and she ate her meal especially slowly. Lingling could only wait patiently. Finally, she saw Grandma stand up, and she followed behind her, calling out, ("Good Grandma, hurry, go quickly!")

Grandma took out four plates of cakes from the food cabinet and placed them on the stone steps near the house in the yard. She also took out an incense burner and two candle holders and placed them in front of them. She also took out a large cup of clear water from the water tank and placed it in a straight line with the three items above. She also folded a hat worn by monks in (Journey to the West) with colorful flower paper and placed it in the center of them.

Her brother stood in front of this (display) and bowed several times, and then dipped his hand in the clear water in the cup and wiped his eyes. Lingling also skillfully did the same, but she bowed two more times.

Grandma gave her more than ten incense sticks, but she thought it was too little and asked Grandma for more. Grandma replied that children cannot stick too many incense sticks, and she only took this much herself. But Lingling thought to herself, "You take less because you are old and can't bend down, but I'm not like you!"

Her brother stuck many rows of incense sticks in the empty flower bed and called her to come and see. She understood that those were some words, and she recited, ("Don't forget that this year is the Year of National Products!") He also stuck many incense sticks in a large radish. A rope was tied to the roots of the radish. He waved this (incense ball), waved it, and waved it on this moonless night, like a shooting star! She looked at it with envy.

Miscellaneous - A Drunkard's Ramblings on Wine 169

— Yu Youqing

Wine is indeed a good thing. When we open Li Bai's poetry collection, we read the line "Drunkenness can dispel ten thousand years of sorrow," which is so fascinating. That's right, wine can dispel sorrow, but to say it can dispel ten thousand years of sorrow is just an old man's boastful language.

"May I ask, where can I find a tavern? A shepherd boy points to Apricot Blossom Village." This poem has been recited by many people. Some people have broken it down: "May I ask, where can I find a tavern shepherd boy, pointing to Apricot Blossom Village." (Changed to a line of different lengths, I think this poem is more interesting.

(Drinking with a bosom friend, a thousand cups are too few). When a close friend suddenly comes, it is really a time to drink and talk happily, and have a heart-to-heart conversation. If it coincides with the saying "meeting an old friend in a foreign land", then it is even more enjoyable.

(When a guest comes at midnight, flowers are used as wine). This saying may refer to rural areas. If it is in a bustling city, then rest assured, when a guest comes at midnight, tea does not have to be used as wine. You can take your guest to the dance hall, and the wine problem can be solved. Even in cities without dance halls, there is no obstacle. You can open a hotel. Don't say you only have wine, even if you want to drink wine and look at flowers, it's very easy.

Wenjun selling wine, Xiangru wearing shorts. This couple unexpectedly fits the modern trend. Widows marrying can be protected by law, and marrying a widow is not a shameful thing. When their love matured, they fled to another place. One held a wine pot as a stove, working as a modern female server and shop assistant, and the other wore the most fashionable shorts to work as a waiter, solving their living problems. Compared with what father-son drug store and brother company, they have cooperated to the end. Xiangru was originally a literary beggar, but for the sake of his lover, he was willing to be a waiter, which is so sincere. It can be said to be an unprecedented great event since the opening of the tavern.

The late Minister of Personnel, Zhuo, was often dismissed from his post for drinking. When the neighbors brewed wine, he would steal a drink. He was tied up by the person in charge of the wine, only to find out in the morning that he was the Minister of Personnel. He was released and asked to get drunk by the jar. This Mr. Zhuo, even after becoming the Minister of Personnel, still wanted to steal other people's wine. He could be said to be a man of refined style, regardless of small matters. With a cup in his hand, everything else was forgotten. ("Everything is inferior to a cup in hand.") When we pass by the door of a wine shop, we see many drinkers holding cups in their hands, with happy faces, which is so beautiful. They feel that with a wine cup in their hand, they don't care about anything else, which fits the saying ("A pot and a bag contain a big universe"). Liu Ling's Ode to Wine is more sincere than the Duke of Zhou's Proclamation on Wine. He couldn't wait for everyone to comb their hair three times after one bath, and spit out their food three times after one meal. No wonder he had to write a Proclamation on Wine. That Mr. Botong saw through everything, loved wine as his life, and wanted to die drunk, so he wanted people to carry a wine jug with him and bury him when he died. This saying is so humorous and profound. Shaw is ultimately inferior to the Wine Saint.

Xinling, fine wine, women. Translating this, it means eating wine and playing with women. Unexpectedly, the current dance halls, opening champagne and playing with dancing girls, have been preempted by that Zhao Gongzi. Originally, wine and sex are two paths that people in the world can hardly escape, especially now that it is an era of revealing flesh, even more unable to see through and jump over. I remember Confucius also said, he said: (I have never seen anyone who loves virtue as much as they love sex.) There is also a saying: (Only wine is limitless, but not to the point of chaos). From this point of view, wine is not necessarily undrinkable, and women are not necessarily unplayable. After all, people who love virtue are fools. The country is in such a state, there is no need to worry about it. It is better to hold a wine glass, hug a dancing girl, or hire a prostitute to serve wine, how interesting. In literary terms, it is called romantic, in colloquial terms, it is romantic. Romanticism fits the modern view of life.

The most famous in the wine country is of course the old Mr. Chun Yuyi. He can eat wine in various ways. One bucket is drunk, and one stone is also drunk, it is a gourd belly that can be big or small. Originally, drinking is a general interest. If one can loosen the collar of the silk robe and faintly smell the fragrance, then at that time, don't say one stone is drunk, even if a few more stones are added, that old gentleman may not necessarily be drunk. This humorous passage in the Historical Records, I want to give to the people who go to dance halls, so that they can get more tips.

Educational News

Jiangsu Province Waives Tuition and Accommodation Fees for Provincial Schools 170

Implemented from the 23rd academic year; other fees will also be reduced. Zhou Fohai, Director of the Jiangsu Provincial Department of Education, noting that students in schools throughout the province were facing heavy burdens, coupled with a faltering social economy, resulting in outstanding but impoverished students being deprived of educational opportunities due to financial constraints, which was a great pity. He proposed to the Provincial Government that, starting from the 23rd academic year, all students in Jiangsu's provincial primary and secondary schools should be exempted from tuition and accommodation fees. The 300,000 yuan in educational funding annually subsidized by the provincial treasury would be incorporated into a special fund to offset the waived tuition and accommodation fees. Due to practical constraints, it was not immediately feasible to implement this for county-run schools and private schools. It was proposed that after the finances were slightly improved, separate plans for offsetting and implementing free education would be considered. It is noted that few provinces currently implement the waiver of tuition and accommodation fees. Zhou's initiative not only provides tangible benefits to impoverished students but also has a significant positive impact on the future of education. It has been learned that the proposal has been approved by the Provincial Government. The original text of the proposal is as follows:

To reduce the economic burden on students, increase educational opportunities for impoverished students, expand education, and enhance its practical effectiveness, it is proposed that provincial primary and secondary schools waive tuition and accommodation fees for students starting from the 23rd academic year. Other fees will also be reduced. All waived fees will be offset by incorporating the existing funds subsidized by the provincial treasury into a special fund to ensure stable income. County-run schools will be addressed separately after financial conditions improve. We would set up a separate panel to plan the subsidies required to implement free education. Please decide on this proposal. Proposed by Zhou Fohai, member and Director of the Department of Education. (Explanation) An investigation reveals that students in schools throughout the province bear tuition, accommodation, and textbook fees, amounting to nearly one hundred yuan for middle school and one or two tens of yuan for elementary school. Families with average financial resources or below are genuinely concerned about their ability to afford these costs. However, in recent years, rural areas have declined, and the rural economy has faltered. It is common to hear of families using their entire year's income, which is insufficient to cover their children's educational expenses, leading to students dropping out or being unable to enroll. Education is a national undertaking, and schools are the state's means of cultivating talent. However, economic constraints cause talented students from impoverished families to be buried, which is not only a loss for individuals and families. In light of this, the Department of Education deeply feels that reducing the financial burden on students' families is an urgent task. Due to practical constraints, it is not immediately feasible to implement this for county-run schools and private schools. It is proposed that after the finances are slightly improved, separate plans will be drawn up to actively plan subsidies and implement free education. It is proposed that provincial schools waive tuition and accommodation fees starting from the 23rd academic year. Other miscellaneous fees collected will be rigorously standardized and substantially reduced to alleviate the burden on students' families and increase educational opportunities for impoverished students. The annual amount of tuition and accommodation fees collected by provincial schools that are included in the budget for offsetting expenditures is approximately 200,000 yuan. It is proposed that this amount be waived, and in the future, the original funds subsidized by the provincial treasury for education be incorporated into this fund to ensure stable income and offset the losses. The provincial education funds from land taxes are set at 1.4 yuan per stone of tribute rice and 4.7 fen per tael of silver. It is proposed that, starting from the collection of tribute rice this year, 2 jiao per stone be added to the item of tribute rice, for a total of 1.6 yuan, to be directly collected by the Education Fund Management Office from various counties for offsetting. This will not increase the burden on the provincial treasury budget but will greatly benefit the practical effectiveness of education. Please approve the implementation if deemed appropriate.

Qingdao Lizhong Normal School Students Strike 171

(Qingdao, 19th) Twenty-four students in the normal school of Lizhong went on strike on the 18th due to poor teaching. They went to the Education Bureau to petition, but there were no results. The students are temporarily staying at the Gaosheng Inn.

Executive Yuan Approves Ministry of Education Proposal on Expenditure Standards for Establishing Secondary Schools 172

(Nanjing, 19th) The Executive Yuan meeting on the 19th approved the Ministry of Education's proposal to establish expenditure standards for establishing secondary schools in various provinces and cities. (1) By the 26th year of the Republic, the allocation of secondary education funds in each province should reach the following standards: Vocational schools should not be less than 35% (including vocational training schools), normal schools should account for approximately 25%, and general middle schools should account for approximately 42%. (2) To achieve the aforementioned standards, starting from the 23rd year of the Republic, any new funding for secondary education in each province should be used primarily for vocational and normal schools. Those that are unable to increase funding should reduce the corresponding amount of funds from general middle schools each year to expand vocational and normal education. (3) When reducing the number and levels of general middle schools, each province must consider the following standards: (1) The average development of secondary education throughout the region, (2) Performance in recent years and examination results, (3) The number of graduates admitted to excellent specialist schools and higher institutions in recent years, (4) Senior high schools should be centrally located in several central locations. If there are two middle schools with senior high school classes in the same location, the senior high school classes should be merged and established separately. (5) The provincial and municipal departments and bureaus are required to prepare a detailed outline plan based on the aforementioned expenditure allocation standards and deadlines before the end of December of the 22nd year of the Republic and submit it to the Ministry for approval. The detailed implementation plan for the 23rd year of the Republic must be submitted for approval before the end of February of the 23rd year of the Republic. After approval, it will serve as the guideline for each province to prepare the budget for educational expenditure in the 23rd year of the Republic. (6) The standards and deadlines listed in item 1 also apply to county and municipal middle schools throughout the province. The departments will plan and supervise their implementation throughout the province. (7) Each department and bureau should strictly examine private middle schools. In addition to banning those with poor equipment and operations, they should also supervise them to convert into vocational schools or vocational training schools, so as to achieve a balanced development of private middle schools and private vocational schools by the 26th year of the Republic. The above measures are carefully formulated in accordance with the central government's long-standing advocacy of promoting productive education and the Ministry's efforts to promote vocational schools, which are crucial to national education. It is requested that all provincial and municipal governments be ordered to strictly comply with them and instruct their subordinates to comply as well.

Details are listed below:

Fudan Overwhelms Yinghua 175

The Fudan volleyball team has dominated Jiangnan for many years. After returning triumphantly from their summer tour of the South, they have not yet assembled for practice. Yesterday was their first battle against Yinghua, and they revealed flaws everywhere. They lost one game to Yinghua. The team's cooperation did not seem to have reached its best. Qiu Guangxie's spikes were indeed powerful. As a result, they eliminated Yinghua with a score of 3 to 1. Today, they will compete against Hujiang in the finals.

Fudan: 20 to 23, 21 to 9, 21 to 6, 21 to 9 Yinghua

Fudan's Unfavorable Start 176

Yinghua served first, taking a 3-2 lead. Fudan added three points to make it 5-3.

There was minor contact between the two sides, but not to a tense point. Yinghua's Huang Zi made a jump serve that violated the rules, making it 7-5, then 10-6. Yinghua repeatedly held the advantage. Fudan launched a fierce attack. Qiu Guangxie tried his long arms for the first time, closing the gap to 8-10, but Yinghua still held the advantage in the first half with 11-8. After switching sides, Qiu Guangxie's fierce kill tied the score at 11. Xie Baochang's high shot missed, and Yinghua once again took the lead, jumping to 18-14, then 20-16. Seeing the unfavorable situation, Fudan quickly chased after them, taking back Yinghua's serve. Zou Bingxin scored on a serve, making it 20 all. They fully intended to strike at the heart of the enemy, but unexpectedly Cheng Mingjue missed a kill, giving Yinghua a match point. At this critical moment, Yinghua's Yang Zhiqiang double-faulted on the serve, tying the score again at 21. In the midst of the chaotic battle, Yinghua's front-row blocking was effective, and Qiu Guangxie's repeated kills were deflected, resulting in the loss of two points. Yinghua thus won the first set 23-21.

Winning the Next Three Sets 177

After a minor setback, Fudan regrouped. Xie Baochang started the serve and scored five points in a row. Yinghua continued to work hard, but couldn't catch up, as Fudan's technique became more proficient and the situation changed. Fudan won the first half of the second set 11-7. Afterwards, Fudan was successful in every aspect, playing with ease, while Yinghua struggled to resist and were at a loss. Fudan retaliated with a 21-9 victory. In the third set, Yinghua appeared even more uneasy, while Fudan's momentum grew stronger. Yinghua only scored two points in the first half. Fudan's Chen Bocai added five points with his serve, and Chen Zongqi served ten times in a row. Fudan then won again with a score of 21-6. In the fourth set, Yinghua rallied their spirits, hoping for a miracle, and took an early lead with 5-1. Fudan did not show any weakness and soon took the lead with 7-5, ultimately taking the lead in the first half with 11-7. The rest of the game belonged to Fudan again. Zou Bingxin also served eight times in a row, and Fudan won again with a score of 21-9, for a total score of 3-1.

Fudan's lineup: Cheng Mingjue, Xie Baochang, Cai Tiange, Zhang Qunguang, Chen Zongqi, Zou Bingxin, Zhou Jieming, Qiu Guangxie, Chen Bohe.

Yinghua's lineup: Lu Xiong, Zheng Zhiyong, Guan Jinlin, Mai Bingguang, Huang Zize, Qu Deming, Jiang Jiayan, Zheng Weiguo, Yang Zhiqiang.

Shanghai University Beats Dongya 178

The Shanghai University volleyball team has a wealth of talent, an organized lineup, and demonstrates excellent coordination in passing and spiking. The back row's defense is solid, the front row's blocking is strong, the setting is accurate, and the middle row of three players can show their skills, delivering powerful spikes. Lu Kangyuan is particularly outstanding, and the other players are also consistently good. It is indeed a strong and complete team, and Fudan will probably find it difficult to deal with. Although Dongya does not have any outstanding players, they put up a strong resistance against Shanghai University with their excellent serves and effective defensive coordination. In the end, Shanghai University won in straight sets, but it was not easy.

Shanghai University 21-15, 23-21, 21-12, Dongya

First Set: Comeback Victory 179

Dongya's Li Daitian served first, but was repelled by Shanghai University, making it 3-0. After 5-2, Dongya scored four consecutive points to take a 6-5 lead. After 6-6, Shanghai University took the lead again at 8-7. Dongya's Huang Peihua made it 9-8. The Shanghai University front and middle rows coordinated well, launching a rapid and fierce attack to gain the advantage. Dongya refused to be outdone and tied the score at 10-10, but Shanghai University took the lead and switched sides at 11-10. Dongya rallied their spirits and put up a tenacious fight, briefly overtaking Shanghai University at 14-12. However, they then collapsed and lost all momentum to Shanghai University. Lu Kangyuan displayed his skills, serving like a cannonball, overwhelming the opposition. Yan Chongji's serve resulted in 21-15 in one breath.

Second Set: Tense Situation 180

Dongya reorganized their forces. Zhu Zhicheng's serves were rapid and forceful, scoring three consecutive points. Shanghai University retaliated, also scoring five points. Dongya advanced to 7-5 and then 9-7, in a rather good situation. Unexpectedly, Shanghai University still took the lead in the first half at 11-9. After switching sides, Shanghai University took the lead. Dongya suddenly found themselves in a pressured situation, but after 15-19, Dongya intensified their efforts, using Tan Xi's powerful serve to disrupt Shanghai University's defense, making it difficult to defend and reducing opportunities for counterattacks, resulting in a tie at 19. However, Tan Xi double-faulted on a serve, ruining all their efforts, and Shanghai University won again with a score of 23-21.

Third Set: Dongya Collapses 181

Since Shanghai University had already won two sets, the overall outcome seemed to be decided. In the third set, Dongya again made mistakes due to panic and lost again with a score of 12-21. After the start, Dongya won two points first. Shanghai University's Yan Chongji served beautifully, adding five consecutive points. Dongya's Huang Peihua showed his strength and retaliated with a heavy spike, tying the score at 5-5. Then Shanghai University's Ruan Shuyiao's serve led to a win in the first half at 11-6. After switching sides and the score being 13-8, both sides displayed their skills in spiking and blocking, showing excellent technique, with an attack and a block going back and forth five or six times, earning thunderous applause. Shanghai University's momentum was strong, and their work became more and more coordinated. Dongya collapsed and lost.

Shanghai University's lineup: Xu Senlin, Lu Kangyuan, Yan Chongji, Wang Jiajun, Huang Jinliu, Li Shufen, Liang Zhihui, Huang Hanming, Ruan Shuyiao.

Dongya's lineup: Yang Dilin, Du Yurong, Tan Xi, Chen Jiongjian, Ling Hongzhao, Zhu Zhicheng, Peng Guangxin, Huang Peihua, Li Daitian.

Jiangsu Provincial Games Opened Yesterday 188

Men's and Women's Shot Put Set New Provincial Records; Huang Zhen of District Eight Scores 9.84 Meters

(Zhenjiang, 19th) The opening ceremony of the Third Jiangsu Provincial Games was held at 8:00 AM on the 19th at the Zhenjiang Public Stadium. Present were Provincial Chairman Gu Zhutong, directors of various departments, guests from various party and government agencies, athletes, and thousands of male and female spectators. First, Wu Bangwei, the Secretary-General of the Games, led the athletes from each district around the field (athletes from District One did not participate). They then proceeded to the podium for a parade and formal greetings. Zhou Fohai, Director of the Department of Education and Chairman of the Games, delivered the opening speech, stating that the purpose of the games was to encourage learning and competition, but not as the ultimate goal. He hoped that participants would pay attention to their usual performance and demonstrate good sportsmanship, rather than focusing on showcasing skills. Shi Shunyuan, from the Provincial Party Headquarters, also gave a speech, followed by an address from the President of the Games, Gu Zhutong. The ceremony ended at 9:30 AM. Then, the Zhenjiang Boy Scout Troop and over 700 male and female students from the Zhenjiang Normal School performed calisthenics. Various competitions began at 10:00 AM.

Lu Ya Xiong Fails to Qualify: Defeated in the 100-Meter Semi-Finals 207

The men's 100-meter preliminary round consisted of five groups of eight people each. In the first group, Liu Rongbo from Zone 1 maintained the provincial record with a time of 12 seconds. The remaining four groups' scores were two at 12.2 seconds, one at 12.7 seconds, and another at 12.8 seconds. Lu Ya Xiong, a Zone 6 athlete who had participated in the provincial games twice and created numerous new records, had recently broken his own Jiangsu province record with a time of 11.8 seconds at the Zone 6 Games. Therefore, when he appeared, the audience watched him intently, with many asking each other, "Which one is Lu Ya Xiong?" However, Ya Xiong's legs betrayed their master in front of everyone, allowing Wang Hongjin from Zone 2 to reach the finish line first by half a head, relegating him to second place. An hour later, the semi-finals began, divided into two groups, with three from each group advancing. Ya Xiong was placed in the second group and failed to qualify. In today's final, Wang Hongjin from Zone 2 has a better chance, but Zhao Congsun from Zone 4 and Liu Rongbo from Zone 1 are also formidable competitors.
